صاحب نتائج نے اس کو حق کہا ہے۔ قوله على ان يعمل معه ... الخ - اس قید کے ذریعہ اس صورت سے احتراز ہے جب غلام کا کام کرنا شرط نہ ہو کہ اس میں تفصیل ہے اور وہ یہ کہ اس صورت میں دیکھا جائے گا کہ غلام کے ذمہ قرضہ ہے یا نہیں۔ سو اگر اس کے ذمے قرضہ نہ ہو تو مضارب کی شرط مذکور صحیح ہو گی۔ خواہ غلام مضارب کا ہو یا رب المال کا ہو۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ غلام کے حق میں شرط مذکور کی تصحیح اس لئے متعدد ہے کہ نفع کا استحقاق یا تو راس المال سے ہوتا ہے یا کام سے یا ضمان عمل سے۔ اور غلام کے حق میں ان میں سے کوئی چیز بھی متفق نہیں ہے۔ لہذا شرط مذکور کو اس کے آقا کے حق میں ٹھہرایا جائے گا( لائ ماهو شرط للعبد شرط لمولاه اذا لم يكن عَلَيْهِ دَين) اور اگر غلام کے ذمہ قرض ہوتو دیکھا جائے گا کہ غلام مضارب کا ہے یا رب المال کا۔ اگر غلام مضارب کا ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک شرط صحیح نہ ہوگی اور مشروط رب المال کے لئے ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں شرط مذکور کی تصیح مضارب کے حق میں بھی متعذر ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مضارب اپنے غلام کی کمائی کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ جب کہ اس کے ذمہ دین ہو۔ البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک شرط صحیح ہوگی اور اس کا پورا کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور اگر غلام رب المال کا ہو تو مشروط بلا خلاف رب المال کے لئے ہوگا۔ (غایہ) قوله ولهذا لا يَكُونُ للمولى.. الخ - يعنی غلام کا قبضہ چونکہ معتبر قبضہ ہے اس لئے آقا کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہوتا کہ غلام نے جو چیز کسی کے پاس و دیعت رکھی وہ اس کو لے لے۔ نیز اسی لئے آقا کا اپنے غلام کے ہاتھ کچھ فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔ جب یہ بات ہے تو شرط مذکور تسلیم مال اور تخلیہ سے مانع نہ ہوگی اور مضاربت صحیح ہو جائے گی۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر مضاربت میں تجارت کا کام رب المال کے ذمہ شرط ہو تو فاسد ہوگی۔ کیونکہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اس سے مضارب کا قبضہ پورا نہیں ہوتا اور تخلیہ کے ساتھ اس کے قبضہ میں مال نہیں پہنچتا۔ بہر کیف جب اس کے غلام کے کام کی شرط لگانا صحیح ہے تو صحت مضاربت کی وجہ سے حسب شرط ایک تہائی نفع مضارب کا ہوگا اور دو تہائی آقا کا۔ کیونکہ غلام کی کمائی اس کے آقا کی ہوتی ہے بشرطیکہ غلام کے ذمہ قرضہ نہ ہو۔
And his statement: 'And the slave of the owner of capital...' - In the book, the restriction mentioned with the slave of the owner of capital is whether it is precautionary or coincidental? Regarding this, the author of Nimah and the author of Mi'raj al-Dirayah said that this restriction is not a condition because the ruling of the slave of the mudarib is also the same. The author of Nihayah quoted details from al-Dhakhirah and al-Mughni that also indicate this. The author of Mi'raj also said that if the mentioned condition is for a stranger, the ruling is still the same; rather, the ruling is the same for every person whose testimony is not accepted for the mudarib or the owner of capital. However, some have written from the Sheikh that the mentioned restriction is because regarding the slave of the owner of capital, there is a difference among some Shafi'is and some Hanbalis, and regarding others there is no difference. The author of Kifayah says: At the time of stipulating work, the slave of the mudarib also has the same ruling; despite that, the restriction of the slave with the owner of capital in the book is intended to remove one doubt, and that is that the possession of the slave is the possession of the master, so it should prevent khaliyah (vacation). So he said it is permissible - the author of Nata'ij deemed this correct. And his statement: 'on condition that he works with him...' - By this condition, the case where the slave's work is not a condition is avoided; there is detail in that, and it is that in that case it will be seen whether the slave has a debt or not. So if he has no debt, then the mentioned condition of the mudarib will be valid, whether the slave belongs to the mudarib or the owner of capital. The reason is that the validation of the mentioned condition for the slave is difficult because the entitlement to profit arises either from capital, or from work, or from guarantee of work, and for the slave none of these exist. Therefore, the mentioned condition will be established for his master (since the condition for the slave is a condition for his master if he has no debt). And if the slave has a debt, then it will be seen whether the slave belongs to the mudarib or the owner of capital. If the slave belongs to the mudarib, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the condition will not be valid and the conditioned benefit will be for the owner of capital, because in this case the validation of the mentioned condition is also impossible for the mudarib, meaning that according to Imam Abu Hanifa the mudarib does not own his slave's earnings when the slave has a debt. However, according to the Sahibayn, the condition will be valid and fulfilling it will be necessary. And if the slave belongs to the owner of capital, then the conditioned benefit will be for the owner of capital without dispute. (Ghayah) And his statement: 'and for this reason the master does not have...' - meaning that because the slave's possession is considered valid, the master does not have the right to take what the slave has deposited with someone. Also, for this reason, the master's sale of something in his slave's hand is permissible. Since this is the case, the mentioned condition does not prevent the delivery of capital and vacation (khaliyah), and the mudarabah will be valid. Contrary to this, if in mudarabah the work of trade is conditioned upon the owner of capital, it will be invalid because it was previously mentioned that this prevents the mudarib's full possession and the property does not come into his possession with vacation. In any case, when stipulating the work of his slave is valid, then due to the validity of the mudarabah, according to the condition one-third of the profit is for the mudarib and two-thirds for the master, because the slave's earning belongs to his master provided the slave has no debt.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses a key issue in mudarabah: can the mudarib or the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) stipulate that a slave (who is involved in the mudarabah) must work? The text first discusses a textual restriction in the original book that mentions 'the slave of the owner of capital'. Scholars differ on whether this restriction is essential (ihtirazi) or coincidental (ittifaqi). Some say it is not a condition because the same ruling applies if the slave belongs to the mudarib. Others say the restriction is to counter a specific doubt: since the slave's possession is actually his master's possession, one might think the slave's presence prevents the mudarib from having full control (takhliyah). The text clarifies that this is not the case; the slave's possession is valid, so the condition is valid. The passage then details the ruling when the slave's work is not stipulated. In that case, if the slave has no debt, the condition (if made) is valid and the profit goes to the master. If the slave has debt, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says if the slave belongs to the mudarib, the condition is invalid because the mudarib does not own the slave's earnings when the slave is in debt; but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid and must be fulfilled. If the slave belongs to the owner of capital, all agree the condition is valid. The passage ends by confirming that the condition does not invalidate the mudarabah because the slave's possession is recognized. The profit distribution follows the condition: one-third to mudarib, two-thirds to master, as the slave's earnings belong to the master.

Key Terms
عبْد (abd): A male slave; in this context, a slave who may be authorised to trade (ma'dhun) or involved in a mudarabah contract.
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave who is permitted by his master to engage in trade; such a slave can contract and be sued in connection with trade.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of capital in a mudarabah contract; the investor who provides funds.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah; the entrepreneur who manages the capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a mudarib stipulates that his own slave (who has debt) must work in the mudarabah, according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The condition is valid and the mudarib must fulfill it.
B) The condition is invalid and the profit from the condition goes to the owner of capital.
C) The condition is invalid and the mudarabah itself becomes null and void.
D) The condition is valid only if the slave's debt is paid off.

Key Takeaway
Stipulating a slave's work in mudarabah is generally valid, but when the slave has debt and belongs to the mudarib, Abu Hanifa invalidates the condition while the Sahibayn uphold it; knowing this ikhtilaf is vital for correct profit allocation.

Cancellation of Mudarabah upon Death and Differences from Agency
Stating ruling with proof then listing exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that mudarabah becomes void upon death of either party and identify three differences between mudarabah and wakalah.

Core Idea
Mudarabah ends at death like agency, but differs in delegation and liability rules.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a core principle: mudarabah is annulled by the death of either the capital owner or the mudarib, drawing an analogy to agency (wakalah). However, the author immediately cautions that mudarabah is not identical to agency in all aspects. To illustrate, three distinct rulings are presented where the two contracts diverge. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying mudarabah law and avoiding confusion with agency.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling and its proof
Identify the primary ruling: mudarabah becomes void (batil) upon the death of either party. Note the proof: it is a form of agency (tawkil), and agency ends with death.
The text explicitly says 'batalat al-mudarabah li-annahu tawkil'.
2
Grasp the analogy and its limits
Understand that the comparison to agency is not absolute. The text cites scholars who explain that in several issues, the rulings differ. This prepares the reader for the exceptions.
Sheikh Itqani and 'Ayni are mentioned as sources.
3
Analyze the first two differences
First difference: In a dispute over returning a defective purchase, the mudarib's refusal to swear keeps the purchase valid, unlike a pure agent. Second difference: A mudarib told 'Work according to your opinion' can delegate to another mudarib, and that delegate can further delegate; an agent told the same cannot delegate beyond one level.
The second difference highlights that the mudarib's authority comes from the contract of partnership, not mere permission.
4
Examine the third difference (agent liability)
The third difference involves a scenario where an agent is given something to buy, and it is lost after purchase. The text is cut off, but the point is that the agent's liability differs from that of a mudarib in similar circumstances.
This difference underscores that agency and mudarabah have independent legal consequences.

Source Text

فَضْلُ فِي الْعَزْلِ وَالْقِسْمَةِ. قَالَ وَإِذَا مَاتَ رَبُّ الْمَالِ اَوِ الْمُضَارِبُ بَطَلَتِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لِأَنَّهُ تَوْكِيلٌ عَلَى مَا تَقَدَّمَ وَمَوْتُ الْمُؤكِلِ يُبْطِلُ الْوَكَالَةَ وَكَذَا مَوْتُ الْوَكِيلِ وَلَا تُؤْرَتُ الْوَكَالَةُ وَقَدْ مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ ترجمہ ( فصل معزولی اور بنوارہ کے بیان میں) جب مرجائے رب المال یا مضارب تو مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایک تو کیل ہے۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا اور موکل کا مرجان وکالت کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اور ایسے ہی وکیل کا مر جانا اور وکالت موروثی نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا۔ تشریح قوله و اذامات اگر رب المال یا مضارب مرجائے تو مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ مضارب کے عمل کے بعد مضاربت توکیل کے حکم میں ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ ہم شروع باب میں ذکر کر چکے اور وکالت موکل یا وکیل کے مرنے سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو مضاربت بھی باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور وجہ دراصل یہ ہے کہ مضارب جو مال میں تصرف کرتا ہے وہ رب المال کی اجازت سے کرتا ہے۔ جیسے وکیل کا تصرف باذن مؤکل ہوتا ہے اور جب رب المال کا انتقال ہو گیا۔ تو اس کی اجازت کتم ہو گئی پس مال غیر من اس کی اجازت کے بغیر تصرف جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح مضارب کے مرجانے سے بھی مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ مضاربت بمنزلہ توکیل کے ہے۔ اور وکیل کا مر جانامبطل وکالت ہوتا ہے اور وکالت وکیل کے ورثہ کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوتی تو ایسے ہی مضاربت بھی منتقل نہ ہوگی۔ قوله لانه توكيل ... الخ - شیخ اتقانی اور عامہ عینی وغیر نے لکھا ہے کہ مضاربت کا وکیل ہونا اصلی کلی کے طرز پر نہیں ہے بلکہ چند مسائل میں مضاربت اور توکیل دونوں کا حکم جدا گانہ ہے۔ پہلا مسئلہ تو وہ ہے جو شیخ الاسلام علاء الدین اسپیجابی نے شرح کافی میں باب شراء الْمُضَارِب و بیعہ “ کے تحت ذکر کیا ہے کہ مضارب نے ایک غلام خریدا اور پھر عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو واپس کرنا چاہا بائع نے اس سے یمین کا مطالبہ کیا کہ وہ اس عیب سے راضی نہیں ہوا تھا۔ نیز جب سے مضارب نے اس کو خریدا ہے اس وقت سے اب تک اس غلام کو فروختگی کے لئے کسی پر پیش نہیں کیا اور مضارب نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو غلام مضاربت پر باقی رہے گا کیونکہ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ ہے کہ یہ معاملہ ابتدائی خرید ہو۔ اور اگر وہ اس کو ابتداء خرید تا تو صحیح ہوتا ایسے ہی استرداد بالعیب کی صورت میں بھی بیح ہو گا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ وہ ہے جو شرح کافی ہی میں "باب المُضَارِبِ يدفع المال مُضَارَبَةٌ " کے ذیل میں مذکور ہے کہ ایک شخص نے مضارب کو مضاربت بالنصف کے طور پر ہزار درہم دے کر کہا۔ اعمل فیہ برا یک ، مضارب نے وہ مال کسی دوسرے کو مضاربت بالثلث کے طور پر دے دیا اور اس نے کام کر کے نفع کمایا تو دوسرے مضارب کے لئے تہائی نفع اور مضارب اول کے لئے چھٹا حصہ اور رب المال کے لئے نصف نفع ہو گا۔ اب اگر مضارب ثانی وہ مال کسی تیسرے کو مضاربت پر دے دے۔ جب کہ مضارب ثانی کے لئے یہ کہا گیا تھا اعمل فیہ برا یک تو وہ اس کا مشارک ہوسکتا ہے اور اپنے مال کے ساتھ خلط بھی کرسکتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر وکیل سے کہا گیا اعمل بر یک تو وہ دوسرے کو وکیل کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر وکیل اول نے وکیل ثانی کے لئے کہا امل فیہ برا یک تو وکیل ثانی کسی تیسرے کو وکیل نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس لئے کہ وکیل اول کو ولایت توکیل اجازت سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور اجازت خاص طور سے اس کے حق میں ہے تو یہ اجازت غیر کے حق میں ثابت نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف مضارب کے کہ اس کو یہ ولایت عقد شرکت کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اعمل فیہ برا یک کہنے کی وجہ سے علی الاطلاق تجارت کا مجاز ہو گیا لہذا جميع انواع تجارات کا مالک ہو گا- وهذا نوع تجارة فملك التفويض الى غيره تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل کو کوئی خریدنے سے پہلے من دیا گیا اور وہ خرید کے بعد اس کے پاس سے تلف ہو گیا تو وکیل اپنے مؤکل سے
Chapter on cancellation and division. He said: When the owner of capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah becomes void because it is an appointment of agency as previously mentioned, and the death of the principal nullifies the agency, and likewise the death of the agent, and agency is not inherited, as previously passed. Translation: (Chapter on cancellation and division) When the owner of capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah becomes void. Because it is a form of agency, as has passed, and the death of the principal nullifies the agency, and likewise the death of the agent, and agency is not inherited, as previously passed. Explanation: He said: 'and when he dies' - If the owner of capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah becomes void. Because after the mudarib's action, mudarabah is in the ruling of agency, as we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter, and agency becomes void by the death of principal or agent, so too mudarabah becomes void. The actual reason is that whatever the mudarib does in the capital, he does with the permission of the owner of capital, just as an agent's actions are with the permission of the principal. When the owner of capital passes away, his permission ceases, so disposing of the property without his permission is not permissible. Similarly, by the death of the mudarib, mudarabah becomes void because mudarabah is like agency, and the death of the agent nullifies agency, and agency does not transfer to the agent's heirs, so too mudarabah does not transfer. He said: 'because it is an agency...' - Sheikh Itqani and 'Ayni and others have written that mudarabah being an agency is not in the absolute general manner; rather, in several issues the ruling of mudarabah and agency differ. The first issue is that which Sheikh al-Islam 'Ala al-Din al-Asbijabi mentioned in Sharh al-Kafi under 'Chapter on the mudarib's purchase and sale': A mudarib bought a slave and then wanted to return it due to a defect; the seller demanded an oath from him that he had not been satisfied with the defect and that since the purchase he had not offered the slave for sale to anyone; the mudarib refused to take the oath, so the slave remains in the mudarabah, because at most it is a new purchase? [text unclear]. And if he had initially purchased it, it would be valid; similarly, in the case of return due to defect, it would be a sale. The second issue is that which is mentioned in Sharh al-Kafi under 'Chapter on the mudarib giving the capital as mudarabah': A person gave a mudarib a thousand dirhams as mudarabah with half share, saying: 'Work with it according to your opinion.' The mudarib gave that capital to another person as mudarabah with one-third share, and he worked and earned profit. Then for the second mudarib one-third profit, for the first mudarib one-sixth, and for the owner of capital half. Now if the second mudarib gives that capital to a third person as mudarabah, when it was said to the second mudarib 'Work with it according to your opinion', then he can become a partner with him and can also mix his own property with it. In contrast, if an agent is told 'Work according to your opinion', he can appoint another agent. But if the first agent said to the second agent 'Work with it according to your opinion', the second agent cannot appoint a third agent. Because the first agent gets the authority of delegation by permission, and permission is specifically for him, so this permission is not established for others. Contrary to the mudarib, who gets this authority due to the contract of partnership, because by saying 'Work with it according to your opinion' he becomes absolutely authorized for trade, so he becomes owner of all types of trade, and this is a type of trade, so he has the right to delegate to others. The third issue is: When an agent is given something to buy before purchasing, and it is lost after purchase, the agent [is responsible?] to his principal...
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This section (Fasl fi al-'Azl wa al-Qismah) begins by stating a fundamental ruling: mudarabah is annulled by the death of either rabb al-mal or mudarib. The reason given is that mudarabah is a form of agency (wakalah), and agency ends with the death of either party. The principle is that the mudarib acts with permission from the rabb al-mal; upon the latter's death, permission ceases, and the mudarib's authority ends. Similarly, the mudarib's death ends the contract because agency is not inheritable. However, the text then clarifies that this comparison does not mean mudarabah is identical to agency in every detail. The author cites Sheikh Itqani, 'Ayni, and others who note that mudarabah only resembles agency in some ways, and in several rulings they differ. Three such differences are then presented. First: In a dispute about returning a purchased slave due to defect, the seller demands an oath from the mudarib; if the mudarib refuses to swear, the purchase remains valid and the slave stays in the mudarabah. This ruling is specific to mudarabah; in pure agency, the ruling might differ. Second: A mudarib who is told 'Work with it according to your opinion' can give the capital to another as mudarabah, and that second mudarib can further delegate to a third because the mudarib's authority comes from the partnership contract and is general. In contrast, an agent appointed with 'Work according to your opinion' can delegate only once; the sub-agent cannot further delegate because the permission is specific to the first agent. Third: The third issue is cut off but involves the agent's liability when goods are lost after purchase. The key point is that despite the general resemblance, mudarabah and wakalah have distinct rulings in these specific cases, and one must not apply agency rules mechanically to mudarabah.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Cancellation or removal of the mudarib by the owner of capital.
قسمة (qismah): Division of profit between the mudarib and rabb al-mal, which becomes necessary upon termination of the mudarabah.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one party authorizes another to act on his behalf.
توكيل (tawkil): The act of appointing an agent or delegating authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the owner of capital dies, what happens to the mudarabah?
A) The mudarabah continues with the heirs of the owner of capital.
B) The mudarabah becomes void because permission ceases.
C) The mudarib has the option to continue until profit is distributed.
D) The mudarabah is temporarily suspended until a new agreement is made.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah becomes void upon the death of either party because it is a form of agency, but it is not identical to agency in all rulings; notably, a mudarib can delegate further while an agent cannot.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Mudarabah Annulled by Death: The Qiyas on Agency
Explains that death of either party annuls mudarabah because it is a form of agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas that mudarabah is void upon death of either party by drawing an analogy to agency (wakalah) and state the underlying illa (effective cause).

Core Idea
Mudarabah ends with death because it is agency by permission; permission dies with the party.

The Hanafi school rules that the death of either the capital provider (rabb al-mal) or the worker (mudarib) immediately voids the mudarabah contract. This ruling is not arbitrary; it is derived through a clear qiyas (analogy) on agency (wakalah). In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning, identify the illa (effective cause), and see why mudarabah is not inheritable.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on death of a mudarabah party
Identify what happens to the mudarabah contract when either the rabb al-mal or the mudarib dies. The ruling is that it becomes void (batil).
The voidness is immediate, not delayed.
2
Identify the analogous contract (asl)
Determine which contract the mudarabah is being compared to. The text explicitly compares it to wakalah (agency).
The analogy is central to the proof.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
Identify the common legal attribute that connects mudarabah and wakalah. The illa is that both are based on permission (idhn) from one party to another to transact.
Permission is personal and ends with death.
4
Apply the ruling from asl to far'
Since wakalah is voided by death of either party, and mudarabah shares the same illa, the ruling is transferred: mudarabah is also voided by death.
This is qiyas jali (clear analogy).
5
Note the consequence regarding inheritance
Understand that the contract does not pass to heirs; it ends completely. The mudarib's heirs do not automatically step in, nor does the owner's heir automatically continue.
The contract is personal, not transferable.

Source Text

A section on the dismissal and division. He said: When the owner of the capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah becomes void because it is a delegation (tawkeel) as previously mentioned, and the death of the principal invalidates the agency, and likewise the death of the agent, and agency is not inherited, and this has passed before. Translation: (A section on dismissal and division) When the owner of capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah will become void. Because this is a delegation. As has passed before, the death of the principal invalidates the agency, and similarly the death of the agent, and agency is not inherited, as has passed previously. Explanation: His statement 'when he dies' - If the owner of capital or the mudarib dies, the mudarabah will become void. Because after the work of the mudarib, the mudarabah is in the ruling of delegation, as we mentioned in the beginning of the chapter. And agency becomes void upon the death of the principal or agent, so mudarabah also becomes void. And the real reason is that the mudarib transacts in the capital with the permission of the owner, just as the agent transacts with the permission of the principal. When the owner passes away, his permission is nullified, so transacting in the property of another without his permission is not permissible. Similarly, with the death of the mudarib, the mudarabah will also become void, because mudarabah is like agency. The death of the agent invalidates the agency, and agency does not transfer to the heirs of the agent, so similarly mudarabah will not transfer.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that mudarabah is annulled by the death of either party. The author explains that mudarabah is a type of agency (tawkeel), and just as agency ends with the death of either the principal or agent, so does mudarabah. The analogy is based on the fact that both parties act by permission. The commentary expands on this by emphasizing that the mudarib's right to transact derives from the owner's permission, and once the owner dies, that permission ceases. Similarly, the mudarib's death ends the contract because it is not inheritable. This ruling is a well-established Zahir al-Riwayah position in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
مضاربت (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, sharing profit as agreed.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one person appoints another to act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does mudarabah become void upon the death of the mudarib?
A) Because the mudarib's work is considered a loan that ends at death
B) Because mudarabah is like wakalah, and agency ends with the death of the agent
C) Because the capital is returned to the owner's heirs
D) Because the mudarib's heirs are automatically entitled to the profit

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is void upon death of either party because it is a contract of permission analogous to agency; permission cannot survive death.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Five Differences Between Mudarabah and Wakalah
Enumeration of five cases where mudarabah and wakalah have different rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state each of the five differences between mudarabah and wakalah and explain the underlying reason for each difference.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is like wakalah but with partnership rights — leading to distinct rulings in delegation, dismissal, and liability.

While mudarabah is fundamentally a form of agency (wakalah), the partnership element gives the mudarib unique rights and obligations. This lesson examines five practical scenarios where the rulings diverge, illustrating how the profit-sharing nature of mudarabah shapes its legal consequences. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the rules of Islamic partnerships.

Guided Path
1
Difference 1: Oath on returning defective goods
Read the first scenario: while a wakeel would be required to swear an oath to return goods due to a defect, the mudarib is not compelled to do so. The reason is that the mudarib's purchase is considered a valid initial transaction, and returning it due to defect does not require an oath.
This highlights mudarib's broader authority in managing the capital.
2
Difference 2: Delegation of work
Study the second scenario: a mudarib can delegate to another mudarib with more flexibility, because his authority stems from the partnership contract. A wakeel's authority to sub-delegate is limited to what is explicitly permitted.
The principle: mudarib has wilayat al-tawkeel by virtue of shirkah, wakeel only by explicit permission.
3
Difference 3: Recovering capital after loss
Analyze the third scenario: if a wakeel receives money from the principal and it is destroyed before purchase, he cannot demand a second payment from the principal. A mudarib, however, can repeatedly request capital because the mudarabah capital is not owned by the mudarib.
This shows mudarib's role as a trustee (amin) with different liability rules.
4
Difference 4: Dismissal after purchase of goods
Examine the fourth scenario: if a mudarib buys goods with mudarabah capital and the principal dismisses him, the dismissal is ineffective until the goods are sold. This is because the mudarib has a right to profit attached to those goods. In wakalah, the wakeel is immediately dismissed upon knowledge.
The mudarib's right to profit makes dismissal conditional upon realization of profit.
5
Difference 5: Effect of apostasy of capital owner
Consider the fifth scenario: if the capital owner apostatizes and goes to dar al-harb, then returns as a Muslim, the mudarabah remains valid. In wakalah, the agency would be terminated upon apostasy, as will be explained later in the text.
The continuity of mudarabah is due to the ongoing partnership interest.

Source Text

سے وابستہ نہیں ہے۔ پانچواں مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر رب المال مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا اس کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر پھر واپس آگیا تو مضاربت علی حالہ باقی رہے گی بخلاف وکالت کے جیسا کہ عنقریب آرہا ہے۔
His statement 'because it is tawkeel ...' - Shaykh Itqani and others have written that mudarabah being like wakalah is not in an absolute sense; rather, in several issues the rulings of mudarabah and wakalah are separate. The first issue: ... [details of five differences] ... The fifth issue: If the owner of capital apostatizes and goes to dar al-harb, then later becomes Muslim and returns, the mudarabah remains as is, unlike wakalah, as will come soon.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage lists five specific scenarios where mudarabah differs from wakalah, despite the general principle that mudarabah is like wakalah. The commentary cites earlier works like al-Kafi. The differences are: (1) A mudarib who buys a slave and then wants to return it due to a defect; unlike a wakeel, he is not required to take an oath. (2) A mudarib can delegate to another mudarib more freely, while a wakeel has restrictions on sub-agency. (3) If money given to a wakeel is destroyed before purchase, he cannot take more from the principal; a mudarib can repeatedly take capital. (4) If a mudarib buys goods and is then dismissed, the dismissal is ineffective until the goods are sold, unlike a wakeel whose dismissal is effective immediately upon knowledge. (5) If the capital owner apostatizes and returns before the judge's ruling, the mudarabah remains valid, unlike wakalah which would be void. These distinctions arise because mudarabah has a partnership element (shirkah) whereas wakalah is pure delegation.

Key Terms
مضاربت (mudarabah): A profit-sharing partnership where one provides capital and the other labor.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; one party authorizes another to act on his behalf.
ولایت توکیل (wilayat al-tawkeel): Authority to appoint a sub-agent; in wakalah it is limited, in mudarabah it is broader.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fourth difference, why is the dismissal of a mudarib ineffective after he has purchased goods with mudarabah capital?
A) Because the mudarib owns the goods personally
B) Because the mudarib has a right to profit from those goods, so he must sell them first
C) Because the dismissal requires a court order
D) Because the mudarib has already completed his work

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah and wakalah differ in five key areas: liability for defects, delegation, capital replacement, dismissal, and effect of apostasy, all due to mudarabah's profit-sharing nature.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Ruling on Apostasy of the Capital Owner in Mudarabah
States ruling on mudarabah apostasy with analogy to death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mudarabah when the capital owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, explain the qiyas to death, and apply the rule that transactions are suspended until judicial confirmation.

Core Idea
Apostasy plus joining dar al-harb voids mudarabah by analogy to death; transactions suspended until judge confirms.

This passage addresses a critical question: what happens to a mudarabah contract when the capital owner leaves Islam and defects to enemy territory? The Hanafi school treats this event as equivalent to death, triggering annulment of the partnership. However, the timing and judicial confirmation introduce important nuances, especially regarding the mudarib's actions during the interim period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the effect of apostasy (irtidad) followed by joining dar al-harb (luhuq) on the mudarabah contract. The ruling is that the mudarabah becomes void (batil).
The annulment is not immediate upon apostasy alone; it requires the joining of enemy territory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is qiyas: joining dar al-harb is like death (bimanzilat al-mawt). The evidence is that the apostate's property is divided among heirs, as in death.
The analogy is based on the legal consequence of property transfer.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to Abu Hanifa, before the actual joining (i.e., before the judge's declaration), the mudarib's transactions are suspended (mawquf). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) likely hold immediate annulment, as implied by the exclusivity of 'inda Abi Hanifah.
This suspension means the transactions are neither valid nor void until the condition is resolved.
4
Understand the effect of return
If the apostate returns to Islam before the judge rules on his joining dar al-harb, the apostasy is deemed never to have occurred, and the mudarabah remains valid with all transactions effective. If he returns after the judge's ruling, the voidance is definitive.
This shows that the annulment is contingent on the judicial determination, not on the act of apostasy alone.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the mudarabah is annulled when the owner does not return before the judge's ruling. The suspension view of Abu Hanifa is the operative position for fatwa, with the condition that return before ruling restores validity.
This is consistent with the principle that apostasy alone does not sever legal ties until legally confirmed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If the owner of capital apostatizes from Islam (we seek refuge with Allah) and joins dar al-harb, the mudarabah becomes void because joining dar al-harb is like death. Do you not see that his property is divided among his heirs? And before his joining, the actions of his mudarib are suspended according to Abu Hanifa, because he acts for him, so it becomes like his own action. Translation: If the owner of capital leaves Islam and joins dar al-harb, then the mudarabah becomes void. Because joining dar al-harb is like death. Do you not see that his property is divided among his heirs? And before his joining, the mudarib's actions are suspended according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Explanation: His statement 'when the owner apostatizes' - If the owner (God forbid) becomes an apostate and goes to dar al-harb, then the mudarabah becomes void. Because due to this, his properties leave his ownership and transfer to his heirs, and his umm walads and others become free, so this is like death. Benefit: There are several cases for this issue: whether he returns to Islam after going or not. If he does not return, mudarabah is void. If he returns, then it depends on whether it was before or after the judge's ruling. If before, mudarabah remains valid and his transactions during apostasy are effective. If after, the mudarabah is void by agreement. A note: In al-`Inayah, etc., it is written that the ruling of annulment in the book applies when the owner does not return to Islam; if he returns, the mudarabah is not void.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of apostasy (irtidad) on mudarabah. The ruling states that if the capital owner (rabb al-mal) becomes an apostate and joins dar al-harb (enemy territory), the mudarabah is annulled, because such action is treated like death—his property is distributed among heirs and his slave concubines become free. However, there is a nuance: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, before the actual joining (i.e., while the apostate is still in dar al-Islam or before the judge declares his joining), the mudarib's transactions are suspended (mawquf), not immediately void. The text further distinguishes cases based on whether the apostate returns to Islam. If he returns before the judge's ruling (i.e., before his joining dar al-harb is confirmed), the mudarabah remains valid and all past transactions are effective. If he returns after the judge's ruling, the mudarabah is void by consensus. This shows that the annulment is contingent on the legal determination of his joining dar al-harb, not merely on apostasy itself.

Key Terms
ارتداد (irtidad): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion.
لحاق بدار الحرب (luhuq bi dar al-harb): Joining enemy territory; a legal construct that severs ties with dar al-Islam and results in treatment like death.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; transactions are held in abeyance pending a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are void and must be redone
B) They are suspended and need approval
C) They are valid and effective
D) They are effective only if the mudarib had no knowledge

Key Takeaway
The mudarabah is void when the capital owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, but transactions before judicial confirmation are suspended and become valid if the owner returns to Islam before the judge rules.

Two Differences Between Mudarib and Wakil: Recourse and Dismissal
Comparing mudarib and wakil in two scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the mudarib from the wakil in terms of recourse rights and the effect of dismissal, and state the legal rationale (ta'lil) for each difference.

Core Idea
A mudarib's right to profit attaches to the goods, so dismissal is ineffective and recourse can be repeated, unlike a wakil whose principal's liability ends after one recourse.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines two key differences between the mudarib (working partner in a mudaraba) and the wakil (agent). The first difference concerns the ability to seek recourse from the capital owner or principal after paying a seller who later dies. The second difference involves the effect of dismissal after purchasing goods. By understanding the underlying rationale—that the mudarib acts for the mudaraba contract and has a right to profit attached to the goods—you will grasp why the rulings differ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two differences being compared
Read the passage carefully. There are two distinct comparisons: (1) recourse after paying the price to a seller who dies, and (2) the effect of dismissal after purchasing goods.
These are separate legal issues, each with its own ruling and rationale.
2
State the ruling for each in mudaraba and wakalah
For recourse: The wakil can seek recourse once, after which the principal's liability ends. The mudarib can seek recourse repeatedly. For dismissal: Dismissal of the wakil is effective upon knowledge; dismissal of the mudarib is ineffective even if he knows.
The mudarib's right is stronger in both situations.
3
Extract the legal rationale (ta'lil) given
The passage provides a reason for each difference. For recourse: the wakil acts for himself, so after one recourse his claim is satisfied; the mudarib does not take for himself but for the mudaraba, and his right is ongoing. For dismissal: the mudarib's right to profit has become attached to the goods, unlike the wakil who has no attachment.
The attachment of right (ta'alluq) is the key concept.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The fundamental distinction is that the mudarib, unlike the wakil, has a proprietary interest in the subject matter (the goods) through the profit share. This interest creates a right that survives dismissal and allows repeated recourse.
This principle also applies in other areas of Hanafi fiqh where a right attaches to property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آنکہ ثمن بائع کو پہنچ جائے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ وکیل اپنے لئے تصرف کرتا ہے اس لئے وہ رجوع کر سکتا ہے اور جب وہ ایک بار رجوع کر چکا تو جو کچھ اس کا کے لئے موکل پر واجب تھا وہ لے چکا اور مؤکل کا ذمہ بری ہو گیا ۔ لہذا اس کے بعد رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ بخلاف مضارب کے کہ وہ مال اپنے لئے نہیں لیتا بلکہ مضاربت کے لئے لیتا ہے۔

پھر شمن لے گا۔ اب اگر وہ بھی ہلاک ہو جائے تو دوبارہ موکل سے نہیں لے سکتا۔ بخلاف مضارب کے کہ وہ رب المال پر بار بار رجوع کرتا رہتا ہے۔

چوتھا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مضارب نے مال مضاربت سے کچھ اسباب خریدا اور رب المال نے اس کو مضاربت سے معزول کر دیا تو اس کا معزول کرنا کارگر نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ مضارب کو اس کا علم ہو جائے بخلاف وکیل کے کہ اگر اس کو معزولی کا علم ہو جائے تو وہ معزول ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ حالت میں حق مضار بہت اس اسباب کے ساتھ وابستہ ہو چکا ہے تا کہ نفع حاصل ہو جس کا حقدار مضارب بھی ہے۔ اور وکیل کا کوئی حق اس سے وابستہ نہیں ہے۔
That the price reaches the seller. The reason is that the agent (wakil) acts for himself, therefore he can seek recourse. When he has sought recourse once, he has taken what was due to him from the principal, and the principal's liability is discharged. Therefore he cannot seek recourse again. Unlike the mudarib, who does not take the property for himself but for the mudaraba. Then he will take the price. Now if that (seller) also dies, he cannot take again from the principal. Unlike the mudarib, who repeatedly seeks recourse from the owner of capital. The fourth issue: that the mudarib purchased some goods with the mudaraba capital, and the owner of capital dismissed him from the mudaraba, then his dismissal will not be effective, even if the mudarib becomes aware of it. Unlike the agent (wakil), who if he becomes aware of dismissal, he becomes dismissed. The reason is that in the mentioned situation, the right of mudaraba has become attached to those goods so that profit may be obtained, and the mudarib is entitled to that profit. And the agent has no right attached to it.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a comparative ruling between mudaraba and wakalah on two points. The first difference concerns recourse after paying the price to a seller who then dies. In wakalah, the agent acts for himself in the sense that he is the one who will be owed by the principal after payment. Once he recovers the amount from the principal upon the seller's death, the principal's liability ends. In mudaraba, the mudarib does not act for himself but for the mudaraba contract. Therefore, if the seller dies, the mudarib can recover the price from the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) repeatedly because the capital owner's liability is not discharged by one payment; the mudarib's right is connected to the profit-sharing. The second difference is about dismissal after purchasing goods. If the mudarib buys goods and then the rabb al-mal dismisses him, the dismissal is ineffective because the mudarib's right to profit has become attached to those goods. In wakalah, the agent has no such right, so dismissal is effective when knowledge reaches him.

Key Terms
مضارب (Mudārib): The person who manages the mudaraba capital; he is the working partner entitled to a share of profit.
وکیل (Wakīl): An agent who acts on behalf of the principal (muwakkil) for his own account in the sense of being entitled to compensation or recovering expenses.
معزول (Ma‘zūl): Dismissed from a position; termination of agency or partnership rights.
رجوع (Rujū‘): Recourse or claiming back expenses from the principal or capital owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a mudarib able to repeatedly seek recourse from the rabb al-mal after a seller dies, unlike a wakil?
A) Because the mudarib acts for himself, so he can keep claiming.
B) Because the mudarib's right to profit is attached to the goods, so the capital owner's liability is not discharged by one payment.
C) Because the mudarib is a partner, so he shares the loss as well.
D) Because the wakil cannot claim recourse at all.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's right to profit attaches to the goods, making his dismissal ineffective and allowing repeated recourse, unlike an agent.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Apostasy of Rabb al-Mal on Mudaraba: Suspension or Immediate Void?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on suspension vs. validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on the effect of the capital owner's apostasy on mudaraba and distinguish between the suspension (tawaqquf) and original authority (wilayah asliyyah) views.

Core Idea
Apostasy of the capital owner does not immediately void the mudaraba; the mudarib's transactions are suspended until the apostate's fate is determined.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the impact of the capital owner's apostasy on a mudaraba contract. The central question is whether the mudarib's transactions remain valid or are suspended between the moment of apostasy and the owner's death or joining dar al-harb. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rulings on suspended contracts (mawquf) and the legal capacity of the agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key events
Recognize two distinct events: apostasy itself and joining dar al-harb. The matn states that joining dar al-harb is equivalent to death, causing the mudaraba to become void. Before joining, the situation is disputed.
The passage also discusses return to Islam before or after a judge's ruling (qada).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that before joining dar al-harb, the mudarib's transactions are suspended (mawquf). If the apostate returns to Islam, they become effective; if he dies or joins, they become void.
His reasoning: the mudarib transacts for the owner, so it is like the owner's own transaction, which would be suspended during apostasy.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the mudarib acts with original authority (wilayah asliyyah) in the mudaraba, so his transactions are valid until an event (death or judicial ruling) terminates the contract.
They do not consider the transactions suspended; they are valid until the contract ends.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference appears when the apostate returns to Islam before a judge's ruling. Under Abu Hanifa, the transactions become effective; under the Sahibayn, they were already valid and remain so. If the apostate does not return, Abu Hanifa voids them retroactively, while the Sahibayn void only from the moment of death or qada.
The text supports the view that after qada, the mudaraba is void by consensus.
5
Note the relied-upon position
The mufta bihi position is that if the apostate returns before the judge's ruling, the mudaraba remains; if after, it becomes void. This reconciles the two views by emphasizing the judge's ruling as the decisive moment.
This is based on the matn's analogy of joining dar al-harb to death and the subsequent commentary.

Source Text

پانچواں مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر رب المال مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا اس کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر پھر واپس آگیا تو مضاربت علی حالہ باقی رہے گی بخلاف وکالت کے جیسا کہ عنقریب آرہا ہے۔

ارتداد رب المال کا حکم
وَإِنِ ارْتَدَّ رَبُّ الْمَالِ عَنِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَالْعِيَاذُ بِاللَّهِ وَلَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ بَطَلَتِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لَانَّ اللِّحَاقَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمَوْتِ الَا تَرى أَنَّهُ يُقَسَّمُ مَالُهُ بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهِ وَقَبْلَ لِحَاقِهِ يَتَوَقَّفُ تَصَرُّفُ مُضَارَبِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَصَرَّفُ لَهُ فَصَارَ كَتَصَرُّفِهِ بِنَفْسِهِ

ترجمہ اور اگر رب المال اسلام سے پھر گیا العیاذ باللہ اور دار الحرب میں مل گیا تب بھی مضارب باطل ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ دارالحرب میں مل جانا بمنزلہ موت کے ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اس کا مال اس کے ورثہ میں تقسیم کر دیا جاتا ہے اور لوق سے پہلے اس کے مضارب کا تصرف موقوف رہے گا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ مضارب کام اس کے لئے کرتا ہے تو اس کے بذات خود تصرف کرنے کی طرح ہو گیا۔

تشریح ..... قوله وان ارتدرب المال اگر رب المال (معاذ اللہ ) مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا جائے ( اور قاضی اس کے لحاق بدار الحرب کا حکم لگا دھے) تب بھی مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے اس کے املاک زائل ہو کر ورثہ کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتے ہیں اور اس کے امہات الاولاد اور بد بر غلام سب آزاد ہو جاتے ہیں تو یہ اس کے مرجانے کے درجہ میں ہو گیا۔

فائدہ ... رب المال کے مرتد ہو کر دارلحرب چلے جانے کے مسئلہ کی چند صورتیں ہیں بایں طور کہ مرتد ہو کر چلے جانے کے بعد وہ پھر مسلمان ہو کر واپس آیا یا نہیں۔ اگر مسلمان ہو کر واپس نہیں ہوا تو مضاربت باطل ہوگئی اور اگر مسلمان ہو کر واپس آگیا تو یہ واپسی قاضی کے لحاق بدار الحرب کا حکم لگانے سے پہلے ہوگی یا اس کے بعد ہوگی۔ اگر واپسی قضاء قاضی سے پیشتر ہو تو مضاربت باطل نہ ہوگی بلکہ علی حالہ برقرار ہے گی۔ اور اس کی ردت کے زمانہ میں مضارب نے خرید و فرخت وغیرہ جو تصرفات کئے ہوں وہ سب نافذ ہوں گے۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس کی ردت اتصال قضاء سے پہلے ہی ٹوٹ گئی تو اس کا حکم باطل ہو گیا۔ گویا وہ مرتد ہوا ہی نہیں اور اگر واپسی قضاء قاضی کے بعد ہو تو بالاتفاق مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ تنبیہ عنایه، بنا یہ کفایہ وغیرہ عام شروح میں لکھا ہے جس کو ان میں سے بعض نے مبسوط کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے کہ کتاب میں جو بطلان مضاربت کا حکم مذکور ہے۔ یہ اس وقت ہے جب رب المال مرتد ہونے کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر واپس نہ آئے۔ اور اگر وہ مسلمان ہو کر واپس آ گیا تو عقد مضاربت علی حالہ برقرار رہے گا۔ خواہ واپسی قضاء قاضی سے پیشتر ہو یا اس کے بعد ہو۔ اگر واپسی قضاء قاضی سے پیشتر ہو تو عدم بطلان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ایسی حالت بمنزلہ غیرو بت کے ہے اور رب المال کی غیبوبت نہ موجب غزل ہے اور نہ موجب بطلان اہلبیت ، اور اگر قضاء قاضی کے بعد ہو تو عدم بطلان مضاربت حق مضارب کی وجہ سے ہے۔ جیسے اگر وہ حقیقۂ مرجائے“۔ (انتھی کلامهم)

صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اس کلام میں اولا تو یہ اشکال ہے کہ اگر وہ حقیقۂ مرجائے تب تو مضاربت یقیناً باطل ہو جاتی ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں مسئلہ گذر چکا پھر یہ کہنا کیسے بیچ ہوا کما لو مات حقیقة ( لا یہ کہ کمالومات حقیقہ کو اس صورت کے ساتھ مقید کیا جائے جب راس المال اسباب ہو کہ اس صورت میں مضارب معزول نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ کتاب میں آگے آرہا ہے۔
ثانیا اس لئے کہ اگر فقہاء قاضی کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر واپسی کی صورت میں عقدِ مضاربت کے بدستور باقی رہنے کی علت حق مضارب ہی ہو تو پھر رب المال کے واپس نہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی مضاربت باقی رہنی چاہیئے۔ کیونکہ حق مضارب جو علت وہاں تھی وہ یہاں بھی ہے۔ پس صحیح بات وہی ہے جو ہم نے فائدہ کے ذیل میں بیان کی ہے کہ اگر رب المال مرتد ہونے کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر واپس نہ ہو یا اس کی واپسی قضاء قاضی کے بعد ہو تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ دونوں میں مضاربت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی تعلیل " لان اللحوق بمنزلة الموت " سے بھی یہی نکلتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب لحوق بمنزلہ موت کے ہے اور موت سے مضاربت باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو ایسے ہی اس سے باطل ہو جائے گی جو منزلہ موت کے ہے اس کے علاوہ بعض دیگر معتبرات سے بھی یہی ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ بدائع میں ہے۔ ولوارتد رب المال فباع الْمُضَارِبِ اور اشترى بالمال بعد الردّة فذلك كله موقوف في قول ابي حنيفة ان رجع الى الاسلام بعد ذلك نفذ ذلك كله والتحق ردّته بالعدم في جميع احكام الْمُصَارَبَةِ وصار كأنه لم يرتد اصلا وكذا اذالحق بدار الحرب ثم عد مسلما قبل ان يحكم بلحاقه بدار الحرب -اهـ
اسی طرح شیخ الاسلام علاء الدین اسمیجابی کو شرح کافی حاکم شہید میں ہے۔ ولوارتد رَبُّ الْمَالِ ثم قتل اومات اولحق بدار الحرب فان القاضي يجيز البيع والشراء على الْمُضَارِبِ والربح له ويضمنه رأس المال في قياس قول ابي حنيفة وقال ابويوسف و محمد هو على المضاربة بالولاية الاصلية فيتوقف ويبطل بالموت او بالقضاء باللحوق ولو لم يرفع الامر الى القاضي حتى عاد المرتد مسلما جاز جميع ذلك على المضاربة لأنَّه انتقضت ردّته قبل اتصال القضاء بها فبطل حكمها اهـ
دونوں عبارتوں میں خط کشیدہ الفاظ سے یہ بات بالکل واضع ہے کہ قضاء قاضی کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر واپس آنے کی صورت میں مضاربت باطل ہوگی۔ قوله وقبل الحوقه ... یعنی رب المال جو مرتد ہوا ہے اس کے لحوق بدار الحرب سے پہلے اس مضارب کے تصرفات (خرید وفروخت وغیرہ) سب امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک موقوف ہوں گے کہ اگر وہ اسلام قبول کرلے تو مضارب کے تصرفات نافذ ہوں گے اور اگر وہ مر جائے یا دت پر قتل کر دیا جائے یا وہ دارالحرب میں مل جائے اور قاضی اس کے لحوق کا حکم کر دے تو تصرفات باطل ہو جائیں گے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مضارب تو تصرف رب المال ہی کے لئے کرتا ہے تو اس کا تصرف رب المال کے تصرف کی طرح ہوا کہ اگر وہ اس صورت میں بذات خود تصرف کرتا تو وہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک موقوف ہوتا پس ایسے ہی اس کے نائب یعنی مضارب کا تصرف بھی موقوف رہے گا۔
Fifth issue: If the owner of capital apostatizes and goes to dar al-harb, then becomes Muslim and returns, the mudaraba will remain as it was, unlike agency as will come shortly. Ruling on apostasy of rabb al-mal: And if the owner of capital apostatizes from Islam (God forbid) and joins dar al-harb, the mudaraba becomes void because joining is equivalent to death. Do you not see that his wealth is divided among his heirs? And before his joining, the transactions of his mudarib are suspended according to Abu Hanifa, because he transacts for him, so it becomes like his own transaction. Translation... Commentary... Benefit: There are several forms of this issue. If he does not return Muslim, mudaraba void. If he returns, it depends on whether the return is before or after the judge's ruling. If before, mudaraba remains; transactions are effective because his apostasy is nullified. If after, by consensus mudaraba becomes void. Note from 'Inayah, Bana'iyah, Kifayah: some attribute to Mabsoot that the voidness ruling is when he does not return. If he returns, the contract remains whether before or after qada? Before: due to being like non-apostasy; after: due to the right of mudarib. The author of Nata'ij objects: if he actually dies, mudaraba is void; so how can they say 'like death'? The correct view is that if he does not return or returns after qada, mudaraba is void. Support from Bada'i' and Sharh al-Kafi: there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa says suspension; they say it is with original authority, so it becomes void upon death or qada of joining. The commentary explains that before joining, transactions are suspended; if he returns Muslim, they are effective; if he dies or joins and judge rules, they become void.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of apostasy of the capital owner (rabb al-mal) on the mudaraba contract. The fifth mas'ala presents the basic ruling: if the apostate returns Muslim, the mudaraba remains. The Arabic text from the matn states that if he joins dar al-harb (after apostasy), the mudaraba becomes void, as joining is analogous to death. Before joining, the mudarib's transactions are suspended (mawquf) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because he transacts on behalf of the capital owner, so it is like the owner's own suspended transactions. The commentary elaborates on multiple scenarios, drawing from various sources. The key dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, before joining (or death), the mudarib's transactions are suspended; they become effective if the apostate returns to Islam, but void if he dies or joins. According to the Sahibayn, the mudarib acts with the original authority, so his transactions are suspended but become void upon death or judicial declaration of joining. The text also discusses the opinion of the author of Nata'ij and quotes from Bada'i' and Sharh al-Kafi. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that if the apostate returns to Islam before the judge's ruling on joining, the mudaraba remains valid; if after, it becomes void. This resolves the apparent contradiction in the earlier note.

Key Terms
ارتداد (Irtidād): Apostasy from Islam by the capital owner (rabb al-mal).
لحاق بدار الحرب (Lihāq bi-dār al-ḥarb): Joining the enemy territory (dar al-harb) after apostasy; legally considered like death in terms of property distribution.
موقوف (Mawqūf): Suspended; transactions are held in abeyance pending a future event (e.g., return to Islam or death).
قضاء قاضی (Qaḍā’ al-Qāḍī): The judge's formal ruling on the apostate's joining dar al-harb, which finalizes the annulment of the mudaraba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the mudarib's transactions if the rabb al-mal apostatizes but dies before joining dar al-harb and before any judge's ruling?
A) The transactions remain valid forever.
B) The transactions become void immediately upon apostasy.
C) The transactions are suspended, and upon death they become void.
D) The transactions are only valid if the rabb al-mal returns to Islam.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's transactions are suspended (mawquf) upon the capital owner's apostasy, becoming effective only if the owner returns to Islam before a judge's ruling on joining dar al-harb.

Effect of Owner's Apostasy on Mudarabah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on mudarabah when owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb: intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the mudarabah contract when the owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, and evaluate the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Joining dar al-harb is like death: after the judge's ruling, the mudarabah is void, even if the owner later returns.

This passage from the Hidayah and subsequent commentaries explores what happens to a mudarabah partnership when the capital owner apostatizes and joins enemy territory. The central dispute is whether the contract remains valid if the owner returns to Islam after a judge's ruling on his joining. We will examine the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and see why the later authorities preferred the view that the contract becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and legal question
The owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb. The mudarib continues transactions. What is the status of the mudarabah?
The scenario involves both apostasy and physical relocation to enemy territory.
2
State the view of Abu Hanifa
Transactions are suspended (mawquf) pending the owner's return. If he returns before the judge's ruling, they are valid; if he dies or the judge rules on his joining, they are void.
3
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)
Transactions are based on original agency, so they are suspended and become void upon death or the judge's ruling. No distinction between return before or after ruling.
4
Understand the critique by the author of Nata'ij
He refutes an earlier claim that the contract remains valid after the judge's ruling, arguing that the analogy to actual death is flawed and the correct analog is voidance.
The critique shows that the 'right of the mudarib' argument is insufficient.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
The contract becomes void after the judge's ruling, supporting the Sahibayn in effect. This is confirmed by Bada'i' and Sharh al-Kafi.

Source Text

مقید کیا جائے جب راس المال اسباب ہو کہ اس صورت میں مضارب معزول نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ کتاب میں آگے آرہا ہے۔ ثانیا اس لئے کہ اگر فقہاء قاضی کے بعد مسلمان ہو کر واپسی کی صورت میں عقدِ مضاربت کے بدستور باقی رہنے کی علت حق مضارب ہی ہو تو پھر رب المال کے واپس نہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی مضاربت باقی رہنی چاہیئے۔ کیونکہ حق مضارب جو علت وہاں تھی وہ یہاں بھی ہے۔ پس صحیح بات وہی ہے جو ہم نے فائدہ کے ذیل میں بیان کی بمنزلة الموت " سے بھی یہی نکلتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب لحوق بمنزلہ موت کے ہے اور موت سے مضاربت باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو ایسے ہی اس سے باطل ہو جائے گی جو منزلہ موت کے ہے اس کے علاوہ بعض دیگر معتبرات سے بھی یہی ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ بدائع میں ہے۔ ولوارتد رب المال فباع الْمُضَارِبِ اور اشترى بالمال بعد الردّة فذلك كله موقوف في قول ابي حنيفة ان رجع الى الاسلام بعد ذلك نفذ ذلك كله والتحق ردّته بالعدم في جميع احكام الْمُصَارَبَةِ وصار كأنه لم يرتد اصلا وكذا اذالحق بدار الحرب ثم عد مسلما قبل ان يحكم بلحاقه بدار الحرب -اهـ اسی طرح شیخ الاسلام علاء الدین اسمیجابی کو شرح کافی حاکم شہید میں ہے۔ ولوارتد رَبُّ یک موقوف ہوتا پس ایسے ہی اس کے نائب یعنی مضارب کا تصرف بھی موقوف رہے گا۔
Book of Mudarabah. The mudarabah contract remains as it is. Whether the return (to Islam) occurs before the judge's ruling or after. If before, the reason for non-voidance is that this state is like being absent, and the owner's absence does not cause annulment nor voidance of the contract. And if after the judge's ruling, the non-voidance of mudarabah is due to the right of the mudarib, like if he actually died. (End of their words). The author of Nata'ij says: In this statement, first there is the problem that if he actually died then the mudarabah definitely becomes void, as the issue has passed earlier. So how can it be said 'as if he actually died' unless it is restricted to the case where the capital is in the form of goods, in which case the mudarib is not removed, as will come later in the book. Second, if the jurists made the cause for the contract remaining after returning to Islam following the judge's ruling the right of the mudarib, then the mudarabah should also remain if the owner does not return, because the same right of the mudarib exists. So the correct view is what we mentioned in the benefit: whether the owner after apostasy becomes Muslim and does not return, or his return is after the judge's ruling, there is no difference. In both cases the mudarabah becomes void. This is also indicated by the author of Hidayah's reasoning 'because joining (dar al-harb) is like death'. Since joining is like death and death voids the mudarabah, so it will be void by what is like death. Aside from that, some other reliable sources also show this. Thus in Bada'i': 'If the owner apostatizes and the mudarib buys and sells with the capital after apostasy, all that is suspended according to Abu Hanifa. If he returns to Islam later, all that is executed and his apostasy is as if it never happened in all rulings of mudarabah, as if he had not apostatized at all. Similarly, if he joined dar al-harb and then returned as a Muslim before the judge ruled on his joining.' Similarly, in Sharh al-Kafi by Sheikh al-Islam 'Ala' al-Din al-Isbijabi: 'If the owner apostatizes and then is killed, dies, or joins dar al-harb, the judge permits the mudarib's buying and selling, the profit goes to the owner, and he is liable for the capital, according to the view of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said it is on the original agency, so it is suspended and becomes void by death or by the judge's ruling on joining. If the matter is not raised to the judge until the apostate returns as a Muslim, all that is valid in the mudarabah because his apostasy was nullified before the judge's ruling reached it, so its ruling is void.' The underlined words in both expressions make it absolutely clear that if one returns as a Muslim after the judge's ruling, the mudarabah becomes void. 'His saying: before his joining' means: before the apostate owner's joining dar al-harb, the mudarib's transactions (buying, selling, etc.) are all suspended according to Abu Hanifa. If he accepts Islam, the mudarib's transactions are effective. If he dies, is killed on apostasy, or joins dar al-harb and the judge rules on his joining, the transactions become void. The reason is that the mudarib conducts transactions for the owner, so his transaction is like the owner's transaction. If the owner himself transacted in that situation, it would be suspended according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, the transaction of his deputy, the mudarib, is also suspended.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the owner's apostasy and his joining dar al-harb on the mudarabah contract. The author of Hidayah (and others) state that the contract remains valid if the owner returns to Islam before a judge's ruling of his joining dar al-harb. However, if the judge rules on his joining, the contract becomes void because joining is like death. The author of Nata'ij critiques an earlier statement that analogizes returning after the judge's ruling to the case of actual death, arguing that actual death voids the contract, so the analogy is flawed. He asserts that the correct position is that the contract is void if the owner returns after the judge's ruling or does not return at all. This is supported by quotations from Bada'i' and Sharh al-Kafi, which present the views of Abu Hanifa and the two students. According to Abu Hanifa, transactions made during apostasy are suspended pending the owner's return to Islam; if he returns, they are effective, but if he dies or joins dar al-harb, they become void. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the agency is original, so transactions are suspended and become void upon death or the judge's ruling. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the underlined words confirm that returning after the judge's ruling voids the contract.

Key Terms
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of the capital in a mudarabah partnership.
مضارب (mudarib): The manager or worker in a mudarabah who invests the capital.
لحاق بدار الحرب (lahaq bi-dar al-harb): The act of an apostate joining enemy territory, legally equated to death in some rulings.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a transaction or ruling that is pending finalization upon a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this text, what happens to a mudarabah contract if the owner (rabb al-mal) apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, and a judge rules on his joining, but he later returns to Islam?
A) The contract remains valid because the owner returned.
B) The contract becomes void and the mudarib's transactions are invalidated.
C) The contract becomes suspended pending the owner's return.
D) The contract becomes valid retroactively to the start of the mudarabah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon position is that a mudarabah contract becomes void when the owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb after a judge's ruling, because joining is legally equivalent to death.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Mudarib's Apostasy on Mudarabah Contract
Ruling on mudarib's apostasy with interpretive commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mudarabah when the mudarib apostatizes and identify the condition that invalidates the contract.

Core Idea
Mudarabah remains valid after mudarib's apostasy, but voids if he joins dar al-harb and a judge rules.

The mudarabah contract is based on trust and mutual capacity to transact. When the mudarib apostatizes, his legal capacity remains intact, so the contract continues. However, if he joins the enemy (dar al-harb) and a judge confirms this, he becomes like a combatant and the contract is void. This lesson unpacks the text from al-Hidayah and the intra-Hanafi debate on this point.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling from the matn
Identify the directly stated ruling: the mudarabah remains on its state when the mudarib apostatizes.
The text uses 'fabaqiyat al-mudarabah' indicating continuity.
2
Identify the two possible interpretations
Recognize that the author of Nata'ij notes two connections for this ruling: either it applies even after joining dar al-harb (Sadr al-Shari'ah's view) or only before joining (preferred).
The second interpretation reconciles with the principle that joining is like death.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The key dalil is the principle 'لأن اللحوق بمنزلة الموت' (joining is like death). This is used to argue that after joining, the mudarib's transactions cease.
This is from the same Hidayah, showing internal consistency.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary sides with the second interpretation, citing Bada'i' and the reasoning of the text. Thus the relied-upon position is that the contract becomes void after joining and a judge's ruling.
The author uses the phrase 'فالصحيح والحق هو الاحتمال الثاني'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ارتداد مضارب کا حکم وَلَوْ كَانَ الْمُضَارِبُ هُوَ الْمُرْتَدُّ فَالْمُضَارَبَةُ عَلَى حَالِهَا لِاَنَّ لَهُ عِبَارَةٌ صَحِيْحَةٌ وَلَا تَوَقَّفَ فِي مِلْكِ رَبِّ الْمَالِ فَبَقِيَتِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ ترجمہ اور اگر مضارب ہی مرتد ہوتو مضاربت اپنے حال پر رہے گی ۔ کیونکہ مضارب کی عبارت ایک صحیح عبارت ہے اور رب المال کی ملکیت میں کوئی توقف نہیں تو مضاربت باقی رہی۔ تشريح ... قوله ولو كان الْمُصَارِبِ بنایہ شرح ہدایہ میں ہے کہ لفظ المرتد دال کے نصب کے ساتھ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ کان کی خبر ہے اور خوشنمیر فصل ہے اور فبقیت الْمُضَارَبَةِ میں فاء کلمہ شرط محذوف کا جواب ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہے واذا كان كذالك فبقيت الْمُضَارَبَةِ على حالها پھر بقول صاحب نتائج صاحب ہدایہ کے قول ولو كان المُضارب هو المرتد فالْمُضَارَبَةِ على حالها میں عقلاً دو احتمال ہیں۔ اول یہ که قول سابق و ان ارتدرب المال ولحق بدار الحرب بطلت المُضَارَبَةِ “ سے وابستہ ہو ۔ اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر مرند مضارب ہو جو دارالحرب میں مل گیا تو مضاربت اپنے حال پر ہاتی ہے یعنی باطل نہیں ہے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ یہ موصوف کے قول و قبل لحوقه يتوقف تصرف مضاربه عند ابی حنیفہ سے پیوستہ ہو اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا۔ کہ اگر مضارب مرتد ہو اپنے لحوق دار الحرب سے پہلے تو مضاربت علی حالہ باقی ہے یعنی اس کا تصرف امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بھی موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ سب کے نزدیک اس کے تصرفات جائز ہیں۔ ان میں سے پہلے احتمال کی طرف صدر الشریعہ گئے ہیں۔ حیث قال في شرح قول صاحب الوقاية وتبطل بموت احدهما ولحاق المالك مرتدا بخلاف لحاق الْمُضَارِب بدار الحرب مرتد احيث لا تبطل المُضَارَبَةِ لان له عبارة صحيحة - اهـ اور متأخرین میں سے صاحب در روغرر اور صاحب اصلاح و ایضاح نے انہی کی پیروی کی ہے۔ اور نفس عبارت وقایہ سے بھی یہی معنی ظاہر ہیں۔ کیونکہ اس مبطل مضاربت موت کو مضارب رب المال میں سے ایک کی طرف علی الاطلاق مضاف کیا ہے اور مبطل مضاربت لحاق کو صرف رب المال کی طرف کیا ہے پس وقایہ کی عبارت اس پر دال ہوتی کہ مضارب کا لحاق مبطل مضاربت نہیں ہے بنابر آنکہ روایات میں کسی شئی کو خاص طور سے ذکر کرنا اس کے ماعداسے حکم کی نفی پر دال ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ فقہاء نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ میرے نزدیک یہ معنی صحیح نہیں اس لئے کہ احکام مرتدین کے باب میں یہ بات ثابت شدہ ہے کہ مرتد جب دار الحرب چلا جائے اور حاکم اس کے لحاق کا حکم کر دے تو وہ اہل حرب ہی سے ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اہل حرب احکام اسلام کے حق میں بالکل مردہ ہیں۔ جیسا کہ صاحب ہدایہ کے قول " لأنَّ اللحوق بمنزلة الموت الا ترى انه يقسم ماله بین ورثته ال سے یہ بات بخوبی واضح ہے۔ اور جب اہلِ حرب بالکل مردہ ہیں تو پھر مردہ کا تصرف کیسے متصور ہوسکتا ہے یہاں تک کہ مضارب کا تصرف علی حالہ باقی رہے جب کہ وہ مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا۔ علاوہ ازیں مضارب کے دار الحرب چلے جانے اور اس کے لحاق بدار الحرب کا حکم ہو جانے کے بعد مضاربت کا باطل ہو جانا تو کتب معتبرہ میں مصرح موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ بدائع میں ہے وان مات الْمُضَارِب او قتل على الردة بطلت الْمُضَارَبَةِ لأن موته في الردة كموته قبل الردة وكذا اذالحق بدار الحرب وقضى بلحاقه لان ردته مع اللحاق والحكم به بمنزله موته في بطلان تصرفه – اهـ پس صحیح اور حق احتمان ثانی ہے اور وہی صاحب ہدایہ کی مراد ہے۔ جیسا کہ مسئلہ کی تعلیل ولا توقف في ملك رَبُّ الْمَالِ " اس کی طرف رہنمائی کر رہی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ قول ملک رب المال میں توقف سے احتراز کے لئے ہے۔ اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جو ملک رب المال میں تو قف ہے وہ لحاق سے پہلے ہے نہ کہ لحاق کے بعد ۔ پس یہاں بھی وہی توقف مراد ہو گا جو لحاق سے پہلے ہوتا ہے. لئلا يلغوا هذا
Ruling on the mudarib's apostasy: 'And if the mudarib is the apostate, then the mudarabah is upon its state, because he has a valid expression (speech) and there is no suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital, so the mudarabah remains.' Translation: If the mudarib apostatizes, the mudarabah remains as it is, because the mudarib's expression is a valid expression, and there is no suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital, so the mudarabah remains. Commentary: His saying 'and if the mudarib' ... In Bina'iyyah Sharh al-Hidayah, the word 'al-murtadd' is in the accusative because it is the predicate of 'kana', and it is a chapter heading. The 'fa' in 'fabaqiyat al-mudarabah' is the answer to a suppressed condition. The implied expression is: 'And if it is so, then the mudarabah remains on its state.' Then, according to the author of Nata'ij, in the statement of the author of Hidayah 'And if the mudarib is the apostate, then the mudarabah is upon its state', there are logically two possibilities. First: it is connected to the previous statement 'And if the owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, the mudarabah is void'. In this case, the meaning would be: if the mudarib is the apostate who joined dar al-harb, then the mudarabah remains upon its state, i.e., it is not void. The second possibility: it is connected to his statement 'and before his joining, the transactions of his mudarib are suspended according to Abu Hanifa'. In this case, the meaning would be: if the mudarib apostatizes before his joining dar al-harb, then the mudarabah remains upon its state, i.e., his transactions are not suspended according to Abu Hanifa either; rather, according to all, his transactions are permissible. Among these, Sadr al-Shari'ah adopted the first possibility, as he said in commentary on the statement of the author of Wiqayah: 'And it becomes void by the death of one of them and by the joining of the owner as an apostate, unlike the joining of the mudarib to dar al-harb as an apostate, because it does not void the mudarabah, as he has a valid expression.' Later scholars like the author of Durar al-Ghurar and the author of Islah wa Idah followed him. And the words of Wiqayah itself indicate this meaning because it attributes the voidance of mudarabah to death absolutely from either party, and attributes voidance by joining only to the owner. Thus the Wiqayah indicates that the mudarib's joining does not void the mudarabah, because in narrations, specifically mentioning something indicates the negation of the ruling from others, as jurists have clarified. However, the author of Nata'ij says: In my view, this meaning is not correct because in the chapter on rulings of apostates, it is established that when an apostate goes to dar al-harb and the ruler rules on his joining, he becomes one of the people of war. And the people of war are completely dead with respect to Islamic rulings. As is clear from the statement of the author of Hidayah: 'Because joining is like death; do you not see that his property is divided among his heirs.' And when the people of war are completely dead, then how can the transaction of a dead person be imagined such that the mudarib's transaction remains as it is when he has apostatized and gone to dar al-harb? Moreover, that the mudarabah becomes void after the mudarib's going to dar al-harb and the judge's ruling on his joining is explicitly stated in reliable books. Thus in Bada'i': 'If the mudarib dies or is killed on apostasy, the mudarabah becomes void, because his death on apostasy is like his death before apostasy. Similarly, if he joins dar al-harb and the judge rules on his joining, because his apostasy with joining and the ruling on it is like his death in the voidance of his transaction.' Therefore, the correct and true possibility is the second, and that is the intention of the author of Hidayah, as indicated by the reasoning of the issue: 'And there is no suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital', because this statement is to avoid suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital. And it is obvious that according to Abu Hanifa, the suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital occurs before joining, not after joining. So here also, the same suspension that occurs before joining is intended, lest this [statement] become meaningless.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the mudarib's apostasy. The core text from al-Hidayah states that if the mudarib apostatizes, the mudarabah contract remains valid because the mudarib's legal expressions (like buying and selling) remain valid and the owner's ownership is not suspended. The commentary then explores two possible interpretations of this ruling in relation to the previous discussion about the owner's apostasy. The first interpretation (adopted by Sadr al-Shari'ah and later scholars) is that even if the mudarib joins dar al-harb, the contract remains valid, unlike the owner's case. The second interpretation (preferred by the author of Nata'ij and the text itself) is that the ruling applies only before the mudarib's joining dar al-harb; after joining and a judge's ruling, it becomes void like the owner's case. The author argues that the text's reasoning (no suspension in the owner's ownership) refers to the situation before joining, not after. Therefore, the relied-upon position is that the mudarabah is void if the mudarib joins dar al-harb and the judge rules on his joining.

Key Terms
عبارة صحيحة (ibarah sahihah): Valid expression; the mudarib's legal capacity to act (buy, sell) remains intact despite apostasy, as long as he has not been killed or judged as a war enemy.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension in ownership; here it refers to the owner's ownership not being suspended by the mudarib's apostasy, unlike the case of the owner's own apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred interpretation in the text, when does the mudarabah contract become void due to the mudarib's apostasy?
A) Immediately upon the mudarib's apostasy.
B) Only when the mudarib dies on apostasy.
C) When the mudarib joins dar al-harb and a judge rules on his joining.
D) It never becomes void; the contract remains valid regardless.

Key Takeaway
The mudarabah remains valid after the mudarib's apostasy unless he joins dar al-harb and a judge confirms his joining, which makes him legally dead and voids the contract.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
