Loss of Mudarabah Capital is Offset Against Profit First
Ruling with proof from qiyas and scenario applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that loss in mudarabah is first attributed to profit, explain the qiyas from zakat, and apply the rule to scenarios involving divided profit and contract termination.

Core Idea
In mudarabah, loss is charged to profit first—the subsidiary bears loss before the principal.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key principle in mudarabah: when capital is lost, the loss is first offset against any profit earned, not the principal. The reasoning draws an analogy from zakat, where loss is first attributed to the exempt portion (afw). This rule protects the principal until profit is exhausted. It also clarifies that if profit was already divided before principal recovery, it must be returned if loss occurs, and that a new contract after rescission is independent of the old profits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The first sentence states that any loss from mudarabah capital is from the profit, not the principal. Recognize this as the foundational rule.
The ruling applies to all losses unless there is negligence (then mudarib is liable).
2
Trace the analogy from zakat
The text justifies the rule by analogy: just as in zakat loss is first attributed to the exempt portion (afw) before touching the zakatable amount, so in mudarabah loss is attributed to profit (the subsidiary) before principal.
The afw in zakat is the wealth below nisab; it is subsidiary to the zakatable portion.
3
Analyze the scenario of divided profit
If profit has already been divided while the contract is ongoing and then a loss occurs, the profit must be returned to cover the loss. This is because division before principal recovery is invalid.
The mudarib is liable for what he took as profit if loss later occurs, but not for the principal loss beyond profit.
4
Distinguish rescinded vs. ongoing contract
If the contract ends and a new one is made, loss in the new contract does not affect previous profit divisions. Each contract is independent.
Analogous to giving a completely new capital.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَا هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ فَهُوَ مِنَ الرِّبْحِ دُونَ رَأسِ الْمَالِ لِاَنَّ الرِّبْحَ تَابِعٌ وَصَرْفُ الْهَلَاكِ إِلَى مَا هُوَ التَّبَعُ أولى كَمَا يُصْرَتْ الْهَلَاكُ إِلَى الْعَفْوِ فِي الزَّكوةِ فَإِنْ زَادَ الْهَالِكُ عَلَى الرِّبْحِ فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَى الْمُضَارِبِ لِأَنَّهُ أَمِينٌ وَإِنْ كَانَـا يَقْتَسِمَانِ الرِّبْحَ وَالْمُضَارَبَةُ بِحَالِهَا ثُمَّ هَلَكَ الْمَالُ بَعْضُهُ أَوْ كُلُّهُ تَرَاذَا الرِّبْحَ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي رَبُّ الْمَالِ رَاسَ الْمَالِ لِاَنَّ قِسْمَةَ الرِّبْحِ لَا تَصِحُ قَبْلَ اسْتِنْفَاءِ رَاسِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَهَذَا بِنَاءٌ عَلَيْهِ وَتَبَعَ لَهُ فَإِذَا هَلَكَ مَا فِي يَدِ الْمُضَارِبِ اَمَانَةَ تَبَيَّنَ اَنْ مَا اسْتَوْفَیَاهِ مِنْ رَاسِ الْمَالِ فَيَضْمَنُ الْمُضَارِبُ مَا اسْتَوْفَاه لِأَنَّهُ اَخَذَهُ لِنَفْسِهِ وَمَا اَخَذَهُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ مَحْسُوبٌ مِنْ رَأْسِ مَالِهِ وَإِذَا اسْتَوْفَى رَأْسَ الْمَالِ فَإِنْ فَضْلَ شَيْءٍ كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ رِبْحٌ وَإِنْ نَقَصَ فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَى الْمُضَارِبِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا فَلَوِ اقْتَسَمَا الرِّبْحَ وَفَسَخَا الْمُضَارَبَةَ ثُمَّ عَقَدَاهَا فَهَلَكَ الْمَالُ لَمْ يَتَرَاذَا الرِّبْحَ الْاَوَّلِ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارَبَةَ الْأُولَى قَدِ انْتَهَتْ وَالثَّانِي عَقْدٌ جَدِيدٌ فَهَلَاكُ الْمَالِ فِى الثَّانِى لَا يُوجِبُ انْتِقَاضَ الْأَوَّلِ كَمَا إِذَا دَفَعَ إِلَيْهِ مَالًا آخَرَ
He said: And whatever is lost from the mudarabah capital is from the profit, not from the principal capital, because profit is subsidiary, and attributing loss to that which is subsidiary is preferable, just as loss is attributed to the exempt amount (afw) in zakat. If the loss exceeds the profit, there is no liability on the mudarib because he is a trustee. And if they have divided the profit while the mudarabah is still ongoing, then the capital is lost partially or totally, they must return the profit until the rabb al-mal recovers the principal, because division of profit is not valid before recovery of principal capital, since it is the origin and profit is built upon it and subsidiary to it. Then when what is in the hand of the mudarib as a trust is lost, it becomes clear that what they took was from the principal capital. Therefore the mudarib is liable for what he took because he took it for himself, and what the rabb al-mal took is counted from his principal. When he recovers the principal, if there is an excess, it is shared between them as profit; if there is a shortfall, there is no liability on the mudarib as we explained. If they divided the profit and rescinded the mudarabah, then entered into a new contract, and the capital is lost, they do not return the first profit because the first mudarabah has ended, and the second is a new contract; loss in the second does not necessitate nullifying the first, just as if he had given him another capital.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with reasoning. The principle is that loss (halak) of mudarabah capital is first attributed to profit because profit is subsidiary to the principal. This is analogous to zakat, where loss is first attributed to the exempt portion (nisab). If the loss exceeds the profit, the mudarib is not liable because he is a trustee (amin). However, if profit has already been divided while the contract is ongoing, and then a loss occurs, the profit must be returned to cover the loss until the principal is restored. This is because division of profit before restoration of principal is invalid. The mudarib is then liable for what he took as profit because he took it for himself. If after recovering the principal there is a surplus, it is profit; if deficit, no liability on mudarib. If the contract was rescinded and a new one made, the loss in the new contract does not affect the old profit, as each is independent.

Key Terms
عفو (afw): The exempt portion of wealth not subject to zakat (nisab).
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss.
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mudarib and rabb al-mal have divided the profit and later a loss occurs while the contract is still in effect, what must happen?
A) The loss is borne by the rabb al-mal alone
B) The profit already taken must be returned to cover the loss
C) The mudarib must return the profit and also compensate for loss
D) The division of profit is final and loss is from capital

Key Takeaway
Loss of mudarabah capital is first offset against profit, and any profit divided before principal recovery is subject to return if loss occurs, but after contract termination, losses in a new contract do not affect prior profits.

Treatment of Capital Loss in Mudarabah
Rulings on loss of capital covered by profit and mudarib's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering capital loss from profit in mudarabah and identify the mudarib's liability.

Core Idea
Loss in mudarabah is first deducted from profit; the mudarib is a trustee, not a guarantor.

This lesson addresses two critical rules in mudarabah: how to handle loss of capital and whether the mudarib bears personal liability. The Hidayah passage, with its supporting proof, clarifies that profit is subordinate to capital, so any loss is first set off against profit. Only after the capital is intact can profit be distributed. If the loss exceeds profit, the mudarib owes nothing because he acts as a trustee (amīn), not a guarantor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
The passage states two rulings: (1) any loss of mudarabah capital is covered from the profit, and (2) if the loss exceeds the profit, the mudarib is not liable.
Ruling 1 applies only when there is profit; ruling 2 applies when loss exceeds profit (or if no profit).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith that compares a believer to a merchant: just as a merchant's profit is not secure until his capital is safe, a believer's supererogatory deeds are not accepted until obligatory deeds are fulfilled.
The hadith is quoted in the Arabic text; its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy implies that profit in mudarabah is contingent upon the safety of capital. Hence, any loss must be compensated by profit before profit can be considered earned.
The logical link is that profit is a branch dependent on the root (capital).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position that the mudarib is not liable for loss beyond profit is based on the principle that the mudarib is an amīn. Other schools, like the Shafi'i, may hold the mudarib liable in certain circumstances.
The khilaf is legitimate; each school has its own evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (muftā bihi) in the school. It is supported by the hadith and the fundamental nature of mudarabah as a trust-based contract.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وما هلك من مال المضاربة يجرى من الربح. إذا مال المضاربة كليا كان أو جزئيا تلف، يجرى ذلك التلف من الربح. لان الربح تابع لرأس المال، فلا يثبت الربح إلا بعد سلامة رأس المال. قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: مثل المؤمن كمثل التاجر لا يسلم له ربحه حتى يسلم له رأس ماله، فكذا المؤمن لا تسلم له نوافله حتى تسلم له فرائضه. قوله لان الربح تابع لرأس المال، لاستحالة بقائه بدون الاصل. قوله فان زاد الهالك على الربح فلا ضمان على المضارب لأنه أمين.
His statement: 'And whatever is lost of the mudarabah capital is covered from the profit.' If all or part of the mudarabah capital is lost, that loss is covered from the profit. Because profit is subordinate to capital, so profit is not established until capital is safe. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The example of a believer is like that of a merchant: his profit is not safe until his capital is safe. Likewise, the believer's supererogatory deeds are not accepted until his obligatory deeds are accepted.' His statement: 'Because profit is subordinate to capital, due to the impossibility of its remaining without the original.' His statement: 'If the loss exceeds the profit, there is no liability on the mudarib because he is a trustee.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage states two rulings regarding loss of capital in a mudarabah contract. First, if any part of the capital is lost, that loss is deducted from the profit before any profit is distributed. The reasoning is that profit is subordinate to capital (رأس المال); just as a branch depends on the root, profit cannot be considered secure until the capital is intact. The author supports this with a hadith comparing a believer to a merchant whose profit is only sound when his capital is sound. Second, if the loss exceeds the total profit, the mudarib is not personally liable for the excess, because he is an amīn (trustee), not a guarantor. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that a trustee is not liable for loss unless there is negligence.

Key Terms
يجرى من الربح (yujrā min ar-ribḥ): The loss is deducted from or covered by the profit; the loss is compensated from the profit before any distribution.
أمين (amīn): A trustee who holds property with permission but is not liable for loss without negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mudarabah capital of 1000 dirhams yields 200 dirhams profit, but then 150 dirhams of the capital is lost, what is the correct distribution?
A) The mudarib must repay the loss from his own pocket, then divide profit.
B) The loss is covered from the profit, leaving 50 dirhams profit to be shared.
C) The loss is ignored and profit is divided normally.
D) The contract is void because of loss.

Key Takeaway
Capital loss in mudarabah is automatically deducted from profit; the mudarib is a trustee and not personally liable for loss beyond profit.

intermediate
8 min
Profit Distribution Before Capital Recovery in Mudarabah
Ruling with analogy to inheritance debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on premature profit division in mudarabah and apply the qiyas with inheritance debt to determine the outcome when capital is lost.

Core Idea
Profit is not owned until capital is secure; premature division is conditional and void if capital is lost.

In mudarabah, partners may be tempted to divide profits periodically. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that such divisions are contingent on the capital remaining intact. If the capital is later lost, the profit distributions are retroactively invalidated, and the profit must be returned to cover the capital. The ruling is grounded in a qiyas with inheritance and debt, where heirs cannot take anything until debts are paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling: If partners divide profit while mudarabah is ongoing, and then some or all capital is lost, the profit must be returned to the capital. The division becomes void.
This ruling applies retroactively.
2
Understand the Rationale
The capital is like a debt owed to the capital owner. Profit is only realized after the capital is fully secure. Until then, any distribution is a premature division of what may turn out to be capital.
The underlying principle is that creditors (capital owner) have priority over profit recipients.
3
Examine the Qiyas
The author draws an analogy: Heirs set aside debt amount, divide remainder, then set-aside is lost; the division is void because debts must be paid first. Similarly, in mudarabah, capital must be intact before profit is taken.
Identify the asl (inheritance case), far' (mudarabah), and illa (priority of right).
4
Apply to Variations
If the mudarib took his share and it is lost, he is liable because he took it as his own. If the capital owner took his share, it is counted as part of his capital, reducing his claim.
Distinction based on who took the profit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان كانا يقتسمان الربح والمضاربة قائمة ثم تلف المال كله أو بعضه رد الربح إلى رأس المال. لأن رأس المال لا يسلم لهم إلا بعد قضاء الدين. فإذا تلف ما في يده تبين أن ما أخذوه من رأس المال. ثم ضرب مثالا: من مات وعليه دين وله تركة، فورثته عزلوا قدر الدين ثم اقتسموا الباقي، ثم تلف ذلك المعزول، فبطله القسمة. لأن الورثة لا يسلم لهم شيء إلا بعد قضاء الدين. فهذا نظير ما نحن فيه. قوله واذا تلف ما أخذ المضارب فإنه يضمنه لأنه أخذه لنفسه وما أخذ رب المال فهو محسوب من رأس ماله.
His statement: 'If they were dividing the profit while the mudarabah was ongoing, then all or part of the capital was lost, the profit is returned to the capital.' Because the capital is not secure until after the debt is paid. So if what is in his hand is lost, it becomes clear that what they took was from the capital. Then he gave an example: someone dies owing a debt and leaving an estate; the heirs set aside the amount of the debt, then divide the remainder; then that set-aside gets lost; the division becomes void. Because the heirs do not secure anything until after the debt is paid. This is analogous to our case. His statement: 'And if what the mudarib took is lost, he is liable for it because he took it for himself; what the capital owner took is counted from his capital.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage addresses a situation where the mudarib and capital owner have been dividing profits periodically during the contract, without first ensuring the capital is fully intact. If afterwards some or all of the capital is lost, those profit distributions are retroactively invalidated. The reasoning is that profit is only realizable after the capital is fully restored. The author draws an analogy with inheritance and debt: heirs cannot secure any inheritance until the deceased's debts are paid; if the set-aside for debt is lost, the earlier division of the estate is void. Similarly, the mudarib's profit share is only his once the capital is safe. Moreover, if the mudarib had already taken his share and that portion is lost, he is personally liable because he took it as his own property, not as a trustee. In contrast, what the capital owner took is reclassified as part of his capital, so it reduces his claim on the remaining assets.

Key Terms
رد الربح إلى رأس المال (radd ar-ribḥ ilā ra's al-māl): Returning the profit to the capital to cover any loss; profit is treated as part of capital when needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qiyas given in the passage, what is the asl (original case)?
A) A mudarabah where capital is lost.
B) An inheritance where heirs set aside debt and divide the rest, then the set-aside is lost.
C) A sale with deferred payment.
D) A loan with interest.

Key Takeaway
Premature profit distribution in mudarabah is conditional on capital being fully secured; if capital is later lost, the distribution is void and profits must be returned to cover the capital.

Effect of Subsequent Loss on Prior Profit Division in Mudarabah
Ruling when profit is divided, contract dissolved, then renewed, and capital later lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a profit division completed in a dissolved mudarabah contract is not affected by a loss in a subsequent contract, and explain the underlying principle of contract independence.

Core Idea
A completed mudarabah contract's profit division stands; later loss in a new contract does not revert it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in mudarabah: after profit is divided, the contract is dissolved, then renewed with the same capital, which is later lost. The question is whether the earlier profit division must be undone. The Hanafi ruling, as stated by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, is clear: the first profit stands. Understanding why requires grasping the independence of each contract once concluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of events
The scenario involves: (1) profit division, (2) dissolution of mudarabah, (3) renewal of mudarabah with same capital, (4) loss of capital. Track each event's legal status.
2
Determine which contract is affected by the loss
The loss occurs under the second contract. The first contract was already dissolved.
3
Apply the principle of contract independence
Hanafi law treats each contract as a separate legal entity. Once a contract is completed (dissolved), its consequences are final. The second contract's loss does not retroactively affect the first.
4
State the ruling and its basis
The ruling: the first profit is not returned. The basis: the first contract was completed (tamm), and the second is new; loss of the new capital does not necessitate annulling the first.
The source says 'العقد الأول قد تم' and 'العقد الثاني جديد'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فلو اقتسما الربح ثم فسخا المضاربة ثم تجددا العقد وتلف المال فلا يرد الربح الأول. لأن العقد الأول قد تم، والعقد الثاني جديد فلا يوجب تلف ماله فسخ العقد الأول.
His statement: 'If they divided the profit, then dissolved the mudarabah, then renewed the contract, and the capital was lost, the first profit is not returned.' Because the first contract was completed, and the second contract is new, so the loss of its capital does not necessitate annulling the first contract.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a scenario: the mudarabah parties divide the profit, then formally dissolve the contract (فسخ). After that, they enter into a new mudarabah contract with the same capital, and then the capital is lost. The question is whether the first profit division becomes void. The ruling is that it does not: the first contract was completed with the profit division being valid at that time (assuming capital was intact then). The new contract is a separate legal entity; its loss does not retroactively affect the completed contract. This is consistent with the principle that each contract is independent once concluded.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Dissolution or termination of a contract by mutual agreement or legal cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The previous profit is forfeited and must be returned.
B) The previous profit is valid and stays with the parties.
C) Only half of the previous profit is valid.
D) The previous profit becomes part of the new capital.

Key Takeaway
The first profit division in a mudarabah remains valid if the contract was completed before dissolution, and a subsequent new contract's loss does not retroactively affect it.

Mudarib's Authority to Sell on Credit
Inter-madhhab dispute on mudarib's credit sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the mudarib's authority to sell on credit and compare it with the opposing view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A mudarib may sell on credit by default because trade custom includes credit — the Quran’s mention of 'present trade' implies 'absent trade' is also trade.

The mudarabah contract grants the mudarib broad authority to conduct trade as customary. This lesson examines whether that authority extends to credit sales without explicit permission from the capital owner. We will analyze the majority view (including Abu Hanifa) and the minority opposition, focusing on the Hanafi proof from the Quran and custom, and conclude with the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the mudarib's default authority: he may sell and buy with cash and credit because it is the practice of traders.
The exception: he cannot sell for a term that traders do not give.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Shurayh, Ibn Abi Layla, and Ahmad (in one narration) require the owner's permission for credit sales.
Their reasoning: credit sales delay return of capital and increase risk.
3
Follow the Hanafi evidence
Examine the two proofs: (1) Quranic verse 2:282 mentions 'present trade' (cash) implying 'absent trade' (credit) is also trade; (2) disallowing credit would cause hardship to the mudarib.
The Quranic inference is from the existence of the term 'present trade' – if only cash were trade, there would be no need to specify 'present'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opponent
The Hanafi school argues that the general contract includes customary practices, and requiring permission for every credit sale would restrict normal business operations.
Custom (urf) is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: under Hanafi, the mudarib can independently decide to sell on credit; under the opposing view, he must seek permission or limit to cash.
This affects the mudarib's operational autonomy and speed of business.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المضارب. قال ويجوز للمضارب أن يبيع ويشتري بالنقد والنسيئة لأن كل ذلك من صنيع التجار فينتظمه إطلاق العقد. إلا إذا باع إلى أجل لا يبيع التجار إليه. وقد اختلف الفقهاء في بيع النسيئة. فذهب أبو حنيفة والشافعي ومالك وأحمد في رواية إلى الجواز. وذهب شريح وابن أبي ليلى وأحمد في رواية أخرى إلى أنه لا يجوز بدون إذن المالك. لنا: أن النسيئة من صنيع التجار، بدليل قوله تعالى: {إلا أن تكون تجارة حاضرة تديرونها بينكم} فالتجارة الحاضرة هي النقد، والتجارة الغائبة هي النسيئة، فدل على جوازها. ولأنه لو لم يجز لضيق على المضارب.
A section on what the mudarib does. He said: 'It is permissible for the mudarib to sell and buy with cash and credit, because all that is from the practice of traders, so the general contract encompasses it. Except if he sells for a term that traders do not sell for.' The jurists differed regarding credit sale. Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad in one narration hold it permissible. Shurayh, Ibn Abi Layla, and Ahmad in another narration hold it impermissible without the owner's permission. Our evidence: credit sale is from the practice of traders, as indicated by the verse: {Unless it is a present trade you conduct among yourselves} so present trade is cash, and absent trade is credit, indicating its permissibility. Also, if it were not allowed, it would cause hardship for the mudarib.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope of the mudarib's authority in transactions. The default rule is that the mudarib can engage in any transaction that is part of ordinary trade, including both cash and credit sales. This is because the general contract of mudarabah gives the mudarib the authority to do whatever is customary among traders. There is an exception: the mudarib cannot set a credit term longer than what traders normally give, as that would exceed customary practice and potentially harm the capital owner. The text then records a dispute: the majority (including Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad in one narration) allow credit sales without explicit permission. A minority (Shurayh, Ibn Abi Layla, and Ahmad in another narration) require the owner's permission. The Hanafi evidence is twofold: (1) credit sales are a standard part of trade, as the Quranic verse indicates that trade can be 'present' (cash) or 'absent' (credit); (2) prohibiting credit sales would impose hardship on the mudarib by restricting normal business operations.

Key Terms
نسيئة (nasī'ah): Sale on credit with deferred payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Yes, but only for a term that traders usually give.
C) No, never.
D) No, but he can if it is urgent.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority to sell on credit is a default permission in Hanafi fiqh, bounded by the customary practices of traders.

Finality of Profit Division After Contract Termination in Mudarabah
States ruling on profit return when contract is cancelled and capital later lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit division after contract cancellation and explain why a subsequent capital loss does not affect it.

Core Idea
A completed mudarabah's profit division is final; a later loss in a new contract does not undo it.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of a new mudarabah's capital loss on a previous profit distribution. The passage clarifies that the first contract is complete, and the new contract stands independently. Understanding this principle protects the finality of contractual distributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of events
There are two mudarabah contracts: the first is completed with profit division and termination; the second begins with new capital and suffers a total loss.
The order of events is critical.
2
Determine the legal status of the first contract
The first contract was properly completed (tam) and terminated; the profit division was a final act of that contract.
A completed contract is binding and closed.
3
Analyze the effect of the second contract's loss
The loss in the second contract does not affect the first because each contract is an independent legal entity.
Contracts are not retroactively linked.
4
State the ruling
The previously divided profit is not returned; it remains with the parties as their rightful earnings.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the underlying principle
The principle is that completed contracts are final and not undone by subsequent events in separate contracts.
This aligns with Hanafi emphasis on contractual stability.

Source Text

Because the first contract of mudarabah was completed, and the second is a new contract; so the loss of capital in the second mudarabah does not necessitate that the first mudarabah's distribution be undone.

Commentary
This is a ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. The passage states that if the mudarib and rabb al-mal divide the profit and then cancel the mudarabah contract, and afterwards they enter into a new mudarabah with new capital, and that capital is lost, the previously divided profit is not returned to the new capital. Why? Because the first contract was fully completed with the division; the second is a fresh contract. The loss in the new contract does not retroactively invalidate the completed first contract. This clarifies that the profit division is final once the contract is terminated.

Key Terms

رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of capital in a mudarabah contract.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital.

Mudarib's Authority to Sell on Credit and Limitations Based on Custom
Expansion of mudarib's credit sale authority with custom limit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib selling on credit, identify the customary limitation, and explain the differences with an agent (wakil) and executor (wasi).

Core Idea
The mudarib may sell on credit only if it is customary among traders; non-customary terms exceed his authority.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines the extent of a mudarib's authority to conduct credit sales. The general rule is permissibility, but it is bounded by the customary practices of traders. The author also distinguishes the mudarib from an ordinary agent and an executor, highlighting the mudarib's broader implied authority stemming from the nature of the partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The mudarib may sell and buy on credit because it is part of trade practice; the general authorization includes it.
The default is permissibility.
2
Apply the customary limitation
If the mudarib sells on a credit term that traders do not normally use, the sale is not permissible. His authority is tied to common custom.
Custom (urf) defines the scope of implied authority.
3
Contrast with agent (wakil) and executor (wasi)
The mudarib can perform iqalah (annulment) and then sell on credit, and accept hawala (transfer of debt), which a wakil cannot. A wasi is restricted to what is best for the orphan.
Mudarib has wider authority due to the nature of partnership.
4
Locate the dalil
The justification is that trade includes credit, and the contract's generality covers customary practices. The verse 'except if it is a present trade...' (Al-Baqarah 2:282) implies credit is permissible.
The proof is from the Quran and the principle of custom.
5
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
Some schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Ahmad) require express permission for credit sales, while Hanafis consider it included in general authority.
The Hanafi view is based on the pervasiveness of credit in trade.

ولو باع بالنقد ثم أخر الثمن جاز بالإجماع أما عندهما فإن الوكيل يملك ذلك فالمضارب أولى إلا أن المضارب لا يضمن لأن له أن يقابل ثم يبيع نسينة ولا كذلك الوكيل لأنه لا يملك ذلك وأما عند أبي يوسف فإنه يملك الإقالة ثم البيع بالنسأ بخلاف الوكيل لأنه لا يملك الإقالة ولو احتال بالثمن على الأيسر أو الأعسر جاز لأن الحوالة من عادة التجار بخلاف الوصي يحتال بمال اليتيم حيث يعتبر فيه الأنظر لتصرفه مقيد بشرط النظر والأصل أن ما يفعله المضارب ثلاثة أنواع نوع يملكه بمطلق المضاربة وهو ما يكون من باب المضاربة وتوابعها وهو ما ذكرنا ومن جملته التوكيل بالبيع والشراء للحاجة إليه والارتهان والرهن لأنه دابة للركوب وليس له أن يشتري سفينة للركوب وله أن يستكريها اعتبارا لعادة التجار وله أن يأخذ إيفاء واستيفاء والإجارة والإستئجار والإبداع والإيداع والمسافرة على ما ذكرناه من قبل
ترجمه مگر جب کہ ایسی میعاد پر بیچے کہ تاجر اس میعاد پر نہیں بیچتے۔ کیونکہ اس کو اسی امور کا اختیار ہے جو تجاروں میں عام معروف ہو۔ اسی لئے وہ سواری کے لئے جانور خرید سکتا ہے۔ اور سواری کے لئے کشتی نہیں خرید سکتا۔ ہاں کشتی کرایہ پر لے سکتا ہے عادت تجار کی وجہ سے اور مضارب کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مضاربت کے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے دے۔ مشہور روایت میں کیونکہ یہ بھی صنیع تجار میں سے ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے نقد فروخت کیا پھر ثمن کو مؤخر کر دیا تو بالاجماع جائز ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ وکیل کو اس کا اختیار ہے تو مضارب کو بطریق اولی ہو گا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ مضارب ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ بیع کا اقالہ کر کے ادھار بیچے کہ مضارب اقالہ کرنے کا پھر ادھار فروخت کرنے کا مختار ہے بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ اقالہ کا مختار نہیں ہے۔ اگر مضارب نے کسی مالدار یا تنگدست پر ثمن کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حوالہ بھی عادات تجار میں سے ہے۔ بخلاف وصی کے جو مال یتیم کا حوالہ قبول کرے کہ اس میں بہتر کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وصی کا تصرف شفقت وبہتری کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ اور اصل یہ ہے کہ مضارب جو کام کرتا ہے وہ تین قسم کے ہوتے ہیں۔ ایک قسم تو وہ ہے جس کا وہ مطلق مضاربت سے مالک ہوتا ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جو باب مضاربت اور اس کے توابع میں سے ہو اور وہ وہی ہیں جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور منجملہ ان کے خرید و فروخت کے لئے وکیل کرنا ہے اس کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے اور رہن لینا، رہن رکھنا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ادا کرنا اور وصول کرتا ہے۔ اور اجارہ پر دینا۔ اجارہ پر لینا۔ ودیعت رکھنا۔ بضاعت دینا اور سفر کرنا ہے۔ بنابر اس تفصیل کے جو ہم نے پہلے ذکر کی ہے۔
A section on what the mudarib does. He said: It is permissible for the mudarib to sell and buy with cash and credit, because all of that is from the practice of traders, so the general authorization of the contract includes it. Except if he sells on a term that traders do not sell on, because he only has authority over what is commonly known among people. Hence he may buy an animal for riding, but he may not buy a ship for riding; he may hire it, paying attention to the custom of traders. And he may take payment and give payment, and hire out and hire, and deposit and entrust, and travel, as we mentioned before. If he sold for cash and then delayed the price, it is permissible by consensus. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the agent (wakil) has that authority, so the mudarib has it a fortiori, except that the mudarib is not liable because he can annul the sale and then sell on credit, unlike the agent who does not have that. According to Abu Yusuf, he has the authority to annul the sale and then sell on credit, unlike the agent. If he accepts a transfer of debt (hawala) on the price from a rich or poor person, it is permissible because hawala is from the custom of traders, unlike the executor (wasi) who accepts hawala on the orphan's property where the better option is considered because his actions are restricted to the condition of welfare. The principle is that what the mudarib does is of three types: a type he has authority over through absolute mudarabah, which is what pertains to mudarabah and its accessories, and that is what we mentioned; included in that is appointing an agent for sale and purchase due to need, and taking and giving a pledge (rahn), because it is an animal for riding and he may not buy a ship for riding but may hire it, and he may take payment and give payment, and hire out and hire, and deposit and entrust, and travel, according to the detail we mentioned before.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on the mudarib's authority. The author explains that the mudarib may sell and buy on credit because this is an ordinary trade practice. However, if he sells on a term that traders do not normally use, it becomes impermissible. The proof is that the mudarib is only authorized for commonly known trade practices. The text then gives examples: buying an animal for riding is allowed (common), but buying a ship for riding is not (common is hiring, not buying); one can hire a ship. The mudarib can also authorize a slave to trade, perform iqalah (annulment) and then sell on credit, accept hawala (transfer of debt), etc. The Hanafi position is supported by the principle that the mudarib's authority is general over trade-related actions. The passage also compares the mudarib with a wakil (agent) and a wasi (executor), noting where the mudarib has broader authority. This clarifies that the mudarib's actions are governed by trade custom, not by individual preference.

Key Terms
النسيئة (al-nasi'ah): Sale on credit with deferred payment.
الإقالة (al-iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract.
الحوالة (al-hawalah): Transfer of a debt from one debtor to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a mudarib sells on a credit term that traders do not normally use?
A) It is permissible because mudarib has full authority.
B) It is not permissible because it exceeds customary practice.
C) It is permissible only if the owner agrees afterwards.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's implied authority to sell on credit is bounded by the trade custom of the place and commodity.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
12 min
Categories of Mudarib's Authority and the Ruling on Deferring Payment
Rulings on mudarib's authority with intra-Hanafi dispute and classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of a mudarib's actions (absolute, conditional, prohibited) and state the ruling on deferring payment after a cash sale, including the intra-Hanafi reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A mudarib can defer payment after a cash sale by consensus, but borrowing (istidanah) is strictly prohibited without express permission.

The mudarib's authority in a mudarabah contract is not unlimited; it is defined by trade custom and the nature of the contract. This lesson examines a key ruling—whether a mudarib can defer payment after a cash sale—and uses it to illustrate a broader classification of his actions into three types. Understanding this classification is essential for determining valid versus invalid actions in mudarabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on deferring payment
The passage states that if a mudarib sells for cash and then defers the price, it is permissible by consensus (ijma'). Identify the act (cash sale followed by deferral) and the ruling (permissible).
This is the main ruling being proved.
2
Trace the proofs (dalil) for permissibility
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue by analogy on a wakil: since a wakil can defer after a cash sale, the mudarib has the same authority a fortiori. Abu Yusuf adds that the mudarib can cancel the sale and then sell on credit, so deferral is a lighter option. Note the qiyas and istihsan reasoning.
The difference in reasoning is intra-Hanafi but the ruling is the same.
3
Understand why the mudarib is not liable
The mudarib does not become liable for the deferred price because he has the option to cancel the sale (iqalah) and resell on credit. If he could do that, then simply deferring is even less consequential. This distinguishes him from a wakil, who cannot cancel.
Liability is a key concern.
4
Learn the three-category classification of mudarib's actions
The passage divides actions into: (1) owned by absolute contract (trade and its necessities), (2) owned only if owner says 'act according to your opinion' (e.g., sub-contracting, mixing funds), and (3) not owned even with that phrase unless explicitly authorized (e.g., borrowing, freeing slaves, gifts). Memorize the categories and examples.
This is a core principle for mudarabah.
5
Apply the classification to istidanah
Borrowing (istidanah) falls into the third category. Even if the owner says 'act according to your opinion', the mudarib cannot borrow because it increases the capital beyond what was contracted. Only explicit permission allows it.
This shows the strict limits on expanding capital.

الْمُضَارَبَةِ فِي التِّجَارَةِ فِي الرِّوَايَةِ الْمَشْهُورَةِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ صَنِيعِ التَّجَّارِ وَلَوْ بَاعَ بِالنَّقْدِ ثُمَّ أَخَّرَ الثَّمَنَ جَازَ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَمَّا عِنْدَهُمَا فَلَانَّ الْوَكِيْلَ يَمْلِكُ ذَالِكَ فَالْمُضَارِبُ أولى إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُضَارِبَ لَا يَضْمَنُ لِأَنَّ لَهُ أَنْ يُقَابِلَ ثُمَّ يَبِيعَ نَسِينَةٌ وَلَا كَذَالِكَ الْوَكِيلُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَّا عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ فَلَانَّهُ يَمْلِكُ الْإِقَالَةَ ثُمَّ الْبَيْعُ بِالنَّسَأَ بِخِلَافِ الْوَكِيلِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْإِقَالَةَ وَلَوِ احْتَالَ بِالثَّمَنِ عَلَى الْأَيْسَرِ أَوِ الْأَعْسَرِ جَازَ لِأَنَّ الْحَوَالَةَ مِنْ عَادَةِ التَّجّارِ بِخِلَافِ الْوَصِيَ يَحْتَالُ بِمَالِ الْيَتِيمِ حَيْثُ يُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِ الْأَنْظَرُ لِأَنَّ تَصَرُّفَهُ مُقَيَّدٌ بِشَرْطِ النَّظَرِ وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ مَا يَفْعَلُهُ الْمُضَارِبُ ثَلَاثَةَ أَنْوَاعِ نَوْعٌ يَمْلِكُهُ بِمُطْلَقِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَهُوَ مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ بَابِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَتَوَابِعِهَا وَهُوَ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَمِنْ جُمْلَتِهِ التَّوْكِيلُ بِالْبَيْعِ وَالشَّرَاءِ لِلْحَاجَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِرْتِهَانُ وَالرَّهْنُ لِأَنَّهُ إِيفَاء وَاسْتِيْفَاء وَالْإِجَارَةُ وَالْإِسْتِجَارُ وَالْإِبْدَاعُ وَالْإِنْضَاعُ وَالْمُسَافَرَةُ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ
ترجمہ مگر جب کہ ایسی میعاد پر بیچے کہ تاجر اس میعاد پر نہیں بیچتے۔ کیونکہ اس کو اسی ہی امور کا اختیار ہے جو تاجروں میں عام معروف ہوں اسی لئے وہ سواری کے لئے جانور خرید سکتا ہے۔ اور سواری کے لئے کشتی نہیں خرید سکتا۔ ہاں کشتی کرایہ پر لے سکتا ہے عادت تجار کی وجہ سے اور مضارب کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مضاربت کے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے دے۔ مشہور روایت میں کیونکہ یہ بھی صنع تجار میں سے ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے نقد فروخت کیا پھر ثمن کو مؤخر کیا تو بالاجماع جائز ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ وکیل کو اس کا اختیار ہے تو مضارب کو بطریق اولیٰ ہوگا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ مضارب ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ بیع کا اقالہ کرکے ادھار بیچے۔ مضارب اقالہ کرنے کا پھر ادھار فروخت کرنے کا مختار ہے بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ اقالہ کا مختار نہیں ہے۔ اگر مضارب نے کسی مالدار یا تنگدست پر ثمن کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حوالہ بھی عادات تجار میں سے ہے۔ بخلاف وصی کے جو مال یتیم کا حوالہ قبول کرے کہ اس میں بہتر کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وصی کا تصرف شفقت وبہتری کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ اور اصل یہ ہے کہ مضارب جو کام کرتا ہے وہ تین قسم کے ہوتے ہیں۔ ایک قسم تو وہ ہے جس کا وہ مطلق مضاربت سے مالک ہوتا ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جو باب مضاربت اور اس کے توابع میں سے ہو اور وہ وہی ہیں جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور منجملہ ان کے خرید و فروخت کے لئے وکیل کرنا ہے اس کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے اور رہن لینا، رہن رکھنا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ادا کرنا اور وصول کرنا ہے۔ اور اجارہ پر دینا۔ اجارہ پر لینا۔ ودیعت رکھنا۔ بضاعت دینا اور سفر کرنا ہے۔ بنابر اس تفصیل کے جو ہم نے پہلے ذکر کی ہے۔
تشریح قوله الا اذا باع الخ- یہ قول سابق "و يجوز ان يبيع" سے استثناء ہے اور بقول علامہ عینی فی نظمہ اطلاق العقد استثناء ہونا بہتر ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مضارب کو ادھار فروخت کرنا جائز تو ہے لیکن اگر اس نے ادھار میں ایسی میعاد قبول کر لی جس پر تاجر لوگ نہیں بیچتے مثلا دس سال کی میعاد پر فروخت کیا تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اس واسطے کہ مضارب کو ایسے ہی امور کا اختیار ہے جو تاجر لوگوں کے یہاں عام طور سے معروف ہوں۔ اور طویل میعاد پر بیچنا تجار کے یہاں معروف نہیں لہذا مالک کی اجازت اس کو شامل نہ ہوگی۔ قوله ولهذا كان له حكم مذکور کی توضیح ہے یعنی اسی وجہ سے کہ مضارب کو صرف انہی امور کا اختیار ہے جو تجار کے یہاں معتاد ہوں۔ سواری کے لئے جانور خرید سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی عادت جاری ہے۔ لیکن سواری کے لئے کشتی نہیں خرید سکتا۔ کیونکہ کشتی خریدنے کی عادت نہیں بلکہ صرف کرایہ پر لینے کی عادت ہے۔ پھر صاحب ہدایہ نے سفینہ کے ساتھ جو لکرپ کی قید لگائی ہے اس کے ذریعے بیچ سے احتراز ہے کہ فروخت کرنے کے لئے کشتی خرید سکتا ہے۔ بشرطیکہ مالک نے کسی خاص نوع میں تجارت کی تخصیص نہ کی ہو۔ اسی طرح مشہور روایت کے مطابق مضارب مضاربت کے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی صنع تجار میں سے ہے۔
قوله في الرواية المشهورة .. الخ - مشہورہ کی قید کے ذریعہ امام محمد سے ابن رستم کی روایت سے احتراز ہے کہ مضارب بطلاق عقد عبد مضاربت کو تجارت کی اجازت نہیں دے سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو مضاربت کے طور پر دینے کے درجہ میں ہے۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مضارب نفع میں شریک ہوتا ہے اور مذکورہ عبد ماذون نفع میں شریک نہ ہوگا۔
قوله ولو باع بالنقد الخ - اگر مضارب نے کوئی چیز نقد فروخت کی پھر مشتری کو ثمن کی مہلت دے دی تو یہ بالاجماع احناف جائز ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک جواز اس لئے کہ جب وکیل کو اس بات کا اختیار ہے کہ نقد بیچ کر مشتری کو ثمن کی مہلت دے دے تو مضارب کو یہ اختیار بطریق اولیٰ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مضارب کی ولایت وکیل کی بہ نسبت عام تر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مضارب نفع میں شریک ہوتا ہے یا شریک ہونے کی عرضیت میں ہوتا ہے پس وہ ایک وجہ سے اصیل ہوا۔ البتہ اتنا فرق ہے کہ مضارب تاخیر ثمن کے بعد رب المال کے لئے ضامن نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ بیع کا اقالہ کر کے مشتری کے ہاتھ ادھار بیچ دے اس لئے کہ جب وہ ابتداء ادھار فروخت کر سکتا ہے تو اقالہ کے واسطہ سے بھی اس کا اختیار ہوگا۔ بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ ایسا نہیں کر سکتا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جواز اس لئے ہے کہ مضارب تو اقالہ کر سکتا ہے۔ پھر مشتری کے ہاتھ ادھار بیچ سکتا ہے تو ثمن میں مہلت دینا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ اقالہ نہیں کر سکتا تو تاجیل ثمن کا بھی مختار نہ ہوگا۔ قوله ولو احتال بالثمن ... الخ اگر مضارب نے کسی مالدار یا تنگدست پر ثمن کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی تاجروں کے یہاں معروف و معتاد ہے۔ بخلاف وصی کے کہ اگر اس نے مال یتیم کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو دیکھا جائے گا۔ کہ یہ یتیم کے حق میں بہتر ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر بہتر ہو۔ مثلاً جس پر حوالہ کیا گیا ہے وہ مدیون سے زیادہ مالدار ہو تو جائز ہوگا ورنہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ جبہ ظاہر ہے کہ وصی کا تصرف یتیم کی بہترائی کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔
وَ نَوْعٌ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ بِمُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَ يَمْلِكُهُ إِذَا قِيْلَ لَهُ اِعْمَلْ بِرَأيِكَ وَهُوَ مَا يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يُلْحَقَ بِهِ فَيَلْحَقُ عِنْدَ وُجُودِ الدَّلَالَةِ وَذَالِكَ مِثْلُ دَفْعِ الْمَالِ مُضَارَبَةً أَوْ شِرْكَةً إِلى غَيْرِهِ وَخَلْطُ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ بِمَالِهِ أَوْ بِمَالِ غَيْرِهِ لاَنَّ رَبَّ الْمَالِ رَضِيَ بِشِرْكَتِهِ لَا بِشِرُكَةِ غَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ أَمْرٌ عَارِضٌ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهِ التِّجَارَةُ فَلَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ مُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَلَكِنَّهُ جِهَةٌ فِى التَّثْمِيرِ فَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ يُوَافِقُهُ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ عِندَ وُجُودِ الدَّالَةِ وَقَوْلِهِ اِعْمَلْ بِرَايِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى ذَالِكَ وَ نَوْعٍ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ لَا بِمُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَلَا بِقَوْلِهِ اِعْمَلْ بِرَايِكَ إِلَّا أَنَّ يَنْصَّ عَلَيْهِ رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَهُوَ الْإِسْتِدَانَةِ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِى بِالدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ بَعْدَ مَا اشْتَرى بِرَأْسِ الْمَالِ السِّلْعَةَ وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَالِكَ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ الْمَالُ زَائِدَا عَلَى مَا الْعَقَدَ عَلَيْهِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ فَلَا يَرْضَى بِهِ وَلَا يُشْغِلُ ذِمَتَهُ بِالدَّيْنِ وَلَوْ أَذِنَ لَهُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ بِالْإِسْتِدَانَةِ صَارَ الْمُشْتَرِى بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ شِرْكَةِ الْوُجُوهِ وَاَخَذَ السَّفَاتِجِ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مِنَ الْإِسْتِدَانَةِ وَكَذَا إِعْطَاؤُهَا لِأَنَّهُ إِقْرَاضٌ وَالْعِتْقُ بِمَالٍ وَبِغَيْرِ مَالٍ وَالْكِتَابَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِتِجَارَةِ وَالْإِقْرَاضُ وَالْهِبَةُ وَالصَّدَقَةُ لأَنَّهُ تَبَرَّعَ مَحْضُ
Mudarabah in trade in the well-known narration because it is from the practice of merchants. If he sold for cash then deferred the price, it is permissible by consensus. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because the agent owns that, so the mudarib is more deserving, except that the mudarib is not liable because he has the option to cancel then sell on credit, and not so the agent because he does not own that. As for Abu Yusuf, because he owns the cancellation (iqalah) then sale on credit, unlike the agent because he does not own cancellation. If he accepted a hawalah of the price on the wealthy or the insolvent, it is permissible because hawalah is from the custom of merchants, unlike the executor (wasi) who accepts hawalah with the orphan's property, where consideration is given to what is more beneficial, because his action is restricted by the condition of benefit. The principle is that what the mudarib does is of three types: a type he owns by the absolute contract, and it is what is from the chapter of mudarabah and its consequences, and it is what we have mentioned, and from it is authorization to sell and buy due to need, and taking and giving in pledge (rahn) because it is payment and receipt, and leasing and hiring, and deposit, and consignment (bida'ah), and travel, as we have mentioned before.
Translation: Except when he sells on a term such that merchants do not sell on that term. Because he has authority only over matters commonly known among merchants. For this reason he can buy an animal for riding, but cannot buy a ship for riding. However, he can hire a ship due to trade custom. And the mudarib has the authority to permit the slave of mudarabah to engage in trade, in the well-known narration, because this is also from the practice of merchants. And if he sold for cash then deferred the price, it is permissible by consensus of the Hanafis. In the view of the two (Sahibayn), it is permissible because the agent has that authority, so the mudarib is more deserving. The only difference is that the mudarib is not liable because he has the option to cancel the sale and sell on credit. The mudarib has authority to cancel and then sell on credit, unlike the agent who does not have authority to cancel. If the mudarib accepted a hawalah of the price on a wealthy or insolvent person, it is permissible because hawalah is from the customs of merchants. Unlike the executor (wasi) who accepts hawalah on the orphan's property, where consideration is given to what is better, because the executor's action is restricted to kindness and betterment. The principle is that what the mudarib does is of three types: one type he owns by the absolute mudarabah, and it is what pertains to the chapter of mudarabah and its dependencies, and they are what we have mentioned, including appointing an agent for sale and purchase due to need, and taking a pledge and giving a pledge because it is payment and receipt, and giving on lease and taking on lease, and depositing, and giving as bida'ah, and traveling, according to the detail we have mentioned before.
Commentary: His saying 'except when he sells' etc. - This is an exception from the previous statement 'and it is permissible for him to sell'. According to Allamah Ayni in his Nazm, it is better that it be an exception from the absolute contract. The meaning is that it is permissible for the mudarib to sell on credit, but if he accepts a term on which merchants do not sell, e.g., he sells on a term of ten years, then it is not permissible. Because the mudarib has authority only over matters commonly known among merchants, and selling on a long term is not known among merchants, so the owner's permission does not include it. His saying 'and for this reason he has the ruling' - clarification of what was mentioned: for this reason the mudarib has authority only over matters customary among merchants. He can buy an animal for riding because the custom exists. But he cannot buy a ship for riding because there is no custom of buying ships, only hiring them. Then the author of Hidayah placed the restriction of 'for riding' with the ship, to avoid the case of selling: he can buy a ship for selling, provided the owner did not specify a particular type of trade. Similarly, according to the well-known narration, the mudarib can permit the slave of mudarabah to engage in trade because this is also from the practices of merchants.
His saying 'in the well-known narration' etc. - By the qualification 'well-known', the narration of Ibn Rustam from Imam Muhammad is avoided, that the mudarib cannot permit the slave of mudarabah to trade by the absolute contract, because this is like giving mudarabah. The difference is that the mudarib shares in profit, but the mentioned authorized slave does not share in profit.
His saying 'and if he sold for cash' etc. - If the mudarib sold an item for cash, then gave the buyer respite for the price, this is permissible by consensus of the Hanafis. In the view of the two (Sahibayn), permissibility is because when the agent has authority to sell for cash and then give respite, the mudarib has this authority a fortiori, because the mudarib's authority is more general than that of the agent, since the mudarib shares in profit or is in the position of sharing, so in one aspect he is a principal. However, there is a difference that the mudarib is not liable to the owner after deferring the price, because he has the authority to cancel the sale and sell on credit to the buyer, and if he can sell on credit initially, he also has authority through cancellation. Unlike the agent, who cannot do that. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, permissibility is because the mudarib can cancel and then sell on credit, so giving respite for the price is also permissible. Unlike the agent, who cannot cancel and thus is not authorized to defer the price.
His saying 'and if he accepted a hawalah on the price' etc. - If the mudarib accepted a hawalah of the price on a wealthy or insolvent person, this is also permissible, because it is also known and customary among merchants. Unlike the executor (wasi), if he accepts a hawalah on the orphan's property, it will be examined whether it is better for the orphan or not. If it is better, e.g., the person on whom it is assigned is wealthier than the debtor, it is permissible; otherwise not. It is obvious that the executor's action is restricted to the orphan's benefit.
And a type which he does not own by the absolute contract, but owns when it is said to him 'act according to your opinion', and it is what can be attached to it, so it attaches when there is an indication. That is like giving the mudarabah or partnership money to another, and mixing the mudarabah money with his own or with another's, because the owner consented to his partnership, not to the partnership of another, and it is an incidental matter that trade does not depend on, so it does not fall under the absolute contract, but it is a means of profit, so from this aspect it agrees with it, so it falls under it when there is an indication, and his saying 'act according to your opinion' is an indication of that. And a type which he does not own neither by the absolute contract nor by his saying 'act according to your opinion', unless the owner expressly authorizes it, and that is istidanah (borrowing), i.e., purchasing with dirhams and dinars after having purchased the commodity with the capital, and the like, because the money becomes in excess of what the mudarabah was contracted on, so he does not consent to it, nor does he encumber his liability with debt. If the owner permits him to borrow, then the purchased item becomes between them half and half, like a partnership of faces (shirkat al-wujuh). And taking suftajahs (bills of exchange) is a type of borrowing, and similarly giving them because it is a loan. And freeing (a slave) for compensation and without compensation, and kitabah (contract of manumission) because it is not trade, and lending, gifting, and charity because it is pure gratuitousness.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya covers several important rulings regarding the mudarib's authority in a mudarabah contract. It begins with the exception that while the mudarib can sell on credit, he cannot do so on an unusually long term that is not customary among merchants. This is because his authority is based on the custom of traders, and an excessively long term exceeds what is commonly accepted. The commentator, using the words of Allamah Ayni, clarifies that this is an exception to the rule of permissibility.

The next ruling concerns the situation where the mudarib sells an item for cash and then gives the buyer a deferment of payment. This is permissible by consensus among the Hanafis. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that since an ordinary agent (wakil) has such authority, the mudarib has it a fortiori because his position is stronger—he shares in profit. However, the mudarib does not become liable for the price because he could have cancelled the sale and sold on credit instead. Abu Yusuf adds that since the mudarib can cancel the sale (iqalah) and then sell on credit, he can also simply defer the payment without cancellation. In contrast, a wakil does not have the authority to cancel, so he cannot defer the payment.

Then the passage discusses the mudarib accepting a hawalah (assignment of debt) for the price from the buyer, whether the buyer is wealthy or insolvent. This is permissible because it is a common practice among merchants. However, the case of an executor (wasi) of an orphan's property is different: the wasi's actions are restricted to what is in the orphan's best interest, so he cannot accept a hawalah unless it is clearly beneficial.

The passage concludes with the fundamental classification of the mudarib's actions into three types. The first type includes actions that are inherently part of trade and its necessary accompaniments—like hiring, pledging, traveling, etc.—and these are owned by the mudarib by virtue of the absolute mudarabah contract. The second type includes actions that are not directly part of trade but are means of profit, such as sub-contracting or mixing funds, and these become permissible if the owner says "act according to your opinion." The third type, like borrowing money (istidanah), freeing slaves, making gifts, or lending, are not permissible even with that phrase unless the owner expressly authorizes them. Borrowing increases the capital beyond what was agreed, and freeing or gifting are not trade. This classification shows the scope and limits of the mudarib's authority within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor for trade, with profits shared as agreed.
حوالة (hawalah): A transfer of debt from the debtor to a third party, which the mudarib can accept on behalf of the partnership.
استدانة (istidanah): Borrowing money to purchase goods after the capital has been exhausted, which the mudarib cannot do without express permission.
إقالة (iqalah): Cancellation of a sale by mutual agreement, which the mudarib has the authority to do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a mudarib defer payment after selling an item for cash?
A) No, because cash sale requires immediate payment and deferral is a new transaction
B) Yes, because the mudarib can cancel the sale and sell on credit, so deferral is even lighter
C) Only if the owner explicitly allows it
D) Yes, but the mudarib becomes liable for the price

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority is not unlimited; deferring payment after a cash sale is permissible by consensus, but borrowing requires explicit permission, and all actions must fall within trade custom.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
6 min
Mudarib's Authority to Authorize a Slave: Own Slave vs. Mudarib Slave
Commentary distinguishing two slave types in mudarabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a mudarib's own slave and a slave who is a mudarib, and state the Hanafi ruling for each regarding authorization to trade.

Core Idea
A mudarib may authorize his own slave for trade, but not a slave who is a mudarib — profit-sharing is key.

This lesson examines a subtle distinction in mudarabah: the mudarib's authority over his own slave versus a slave who is a mudarib. The Hanafi school, based on the famous narration of Imam Muhammad, holds that while a mudarib can authorize his personal slave for trade, he cannot authorize a slave who has been appointed as a mudarib by someone else. The reasoning lies in the nature of mudarabah and profit-sharing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and note the two scenarios: (1) mudarib's own slave, (2) slave who himself is a mudarib (ʿabd mudārabah).
2
State the ruling for each
The mudarib may authorize his own slave for trade. According to the famous narration, he may not authorize a slave who is a mudarib.
3
Understand the rationale
The mudarib shares in profit, but an authorized slave (maʾdhūn) does not. Authorizing a mudarib slave would effectively transfer mudarabah without profit-sharing.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Ibn Rustam's narration from Imam Muhammad permits authorizing a mudarib slave, but the famous narration (riwāyah mashhūrah) is preferred and relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی مصنیع تجار میں سے ہے۔ قوله في الرواية المشهورة .. الخ - مشہورہ کی قید کے ذریعہ امام محمد سے ابن رستم کی روایت سے احتراز ہے کہ مضارب با طلاق عقد عبد مضاربت کو تجارت کی اجازت نہیں دے سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو مضاربت کے طور پر دینے کے درجہ میں ہے۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مضارب نفع میں شریک ہوتا ہے اور مذکورہ عبد ماذون نفع میں شریک نہ ہوگا۔
He can authorize his slave for trade because he is also among the skilled traders. His statement: 'according to the famous narration' etc. - By the restriction 'famous narration', the narration of Ibn Rustam from Imam Muhammad is avoided, that the mudarib cannot authorize a slave who is a mudarib to trade, because it is like giving on the basis of mudarabah. The reason for the difference is that the mudarib shares in profit, while the mentioned authorized slave will not share in profit.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that a mudarib can authorize his own slave for trade, and then distinguishes the case of a slave who is himself a mudarib. According to the famous narration (riwayah mashhurah from Imam Muhammad), the mudarib cannot give trade permission to a slave who has been appointed as a mudarib by another person, because that would effectively be transferring the mudarabah to the slave without the profit-sharing arrangement. The slave, being merely authorized (mawzoon), does not share in profit, whereas the mudarib does. The difference in nature prevents this authorization.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The active partner in a mudarabah contract who invests labor.
عبد مضاربت (ʿabd mudārabah): A slave who has been given capital on mudarabah by someone else.
ماذون (maʾdhūn): A slave given permission to trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a mudarib authorize a slave who is himself a mudarib to trade with the mudarabah capital?
A) Yes, because he is a skilled trader.
B) No, because that would be like giving mudarabah without profit share.
C) Only if the slave agrees.
D) Only if the rabb al-mal permits.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib cannot authorize a slave who is a mudarib because the essential profit-sharing element is missing.

Mudarib Giving Respite After Cash Sale
Ruling on mudarib granting respite after cash sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that a mudarib may grant respite after a cash sale, and distinguish his authority from that of a wakil.

Core Idea
A mudarib's authority exceeds a wakil's, so he can give payment extensions and even rescind and resell on credit.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies the scope of a mudarib's authority after a cash sale. While a simple agent (wakil) cannot change payment terms post-sale, the mudarib, due to his profit-sharing role, has wider discretion. The ruling is established by consensus and supported by a fortiori analogy and the unique ability to rescind the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Mudarib giving buyer respite after a cash sale). What is the hukm? (Jaiz/permissible by consensus).
The consensus includes all three Hanafi imams despite differing reasoning.
2
Understand the qiyas to wakil
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue: if a wakil can give respite, a mudarib can do so more (awlawiyyah) because his authority is broader due to profit sharing.
3
Examine the iqalah dimension
The mudarib has a unique tool: he can cancel the sale (iqalah) and then sell on credit. This is why he is not liable after giving respite, unlike a wakil.
Imam Abu Yusuf's reasoning focuses solely on this iqalah ability.
4
Compare the two justifications
Note that both reasoning paths lead to the same ruling: permissibility. The practical difference is the scope of the argument, not the outcome.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Can a mudarib give a buyer extra time after a cash sale without rabb al-mal's consent? Yes, by this ruling.
This contrasts with a wakil, who would need consent or is barred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو باع بالنقد الخ - اگر مضارب نے کوئی چیز نقد فروخت کی پھر مشتری کو شمن کی مہلت دے دی تو یہ با جماع احناف جائز ہے۔۔ طرفین کے نزدیک تو جواز اس لئے کہ جب وکیل کو اس بات کا اختیار ہے کہ نقد بیچ کرمشتری کوشن کی مہلت دے دے تو مضارب کو یہ اختیار بطریق اولی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مضارب کی ولایت وکیل کی بہ نسبت عام تر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مضارب نفع میں شریک ہوتا ہے یا شریک ہونے کی عرضیت میں ہوتا ہے پس وہ ایک وجہ سے اصیل ہوا۔ البتہ اتنا فرق ہے کہ مضارب تاخیر ثمن کے بعد رب المال کے لئے ضامن نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ بیج کا اقالہ کر کے مشتری کے ہاتھ ادھار بیچ دے اس لئے کہ جب وہ ابتداء ادھار فروخت کر سکتا ہے تو اقالہ کے واسطہ سے بھی اس کا اختیار ہوگا۔ بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ ایسا نہیں کر سکتا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جواز اس لئے ہے کہ مضارب تو اقالہ کر سکتا ہے۔ پھر مشتری کے ہاتھ ادھار بیچ سکتا ہے تو شمن میں مہلت دینا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ بخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ اقالہ نہیں کر سکتا تو تاجیل شمن کا بھی مختار نہ ہوگا۔
His statement: 'And if he sold for cash etc.' - If the mudarib sold something for cash, then gave the buyer respite for the price, this is permissible by consensus of the Hanafis. According to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?), the permissibility is because when a wakil has the authority to sell for cash and then give respite, the mudarib has this authority more so, because the mudarib's authority is more general than that of a wakil. This is because the mudarib shares in profit or is on the verge of sharing, so he is in one respect an agent. However, there is a difference: the mudarib is not liable for the price after delay because he has the authority to cancel the sale (iqalah) and then sell on credit, since he can sell on credit initially, so he also has authority through iqalah. Unlike the wakil, who cannot do that. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the permissibility is because the mudarib can make iqalah and then sell on credit, so giving respite is also permissible. Unlike the wakil, who cannot make iqalah, so he is not authorized to give respite.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses a ruling: if a mudarib sells goods for cash and then gives the buyer more time to pay, it is valid by consensus of the Hanafi school. The reasoning is analogical: a wakil (agent) has the authority to sell for cash and subsequently give respite, and the mudarib's authority is even broader because he has a stake in profit, making him like a principal in some respects. However, a key difference is that after giving respite, the mudarib is not liable for the price because he can cancel the sale (iqalah) and then sell on credit—a flexibility not available to a wakil. Imam Abu Yusuf's justification relies on the mudarib's ability to perform iqalah, which the wakil lacks.

Key Terms
اقالہ (iqālah): Mutual rescission of a contract.
تاجیل ثمن (taʿjīl al-thaman): Giving respite for payment of the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a mudarib, after selling goods for cash, give the buyer extra time to pay?
A) Yes, but only if the rabb al-mal agrees.
B) Yes, because his authority is broader than a wakil.
C) No, because the sale is final.
D) No, only a wakil can do that.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib may unilaterally extend payment terms after a cash sale, reflecting his broader agency due to profit sharing and the ability to rescind and recontract.

Mudarib's Authority: Accepting Hawala
Ruling on mudarib accepting hawala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib accepting hawala, explain the difference between mudarib and wasi in this context, and apply the condition of 'urf (custom) as a proof.

Core Idea
A mudarib can accept hawala freely; a wasi must ensure the orphan's benefit.

In this passage, the Hidayah author compares the mudarib’s authority to accept a hawala (debt transfer) with that of a wasi (guardian of an orphan). The mudarib is allowed because it is customary among traders, while the wasi is restricted by the requirement of benefit for the orphan. Understanding this distinction clarifies the limits of agency in Hanafi muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Mudarib accepting hawala for the price). What is the hukm (permissible)?
The ruling is jāʾiz (permissible) for both wealthy and poor drawees.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What proof does the author cite? (Custom of traders – 'urf). Why is this a valid proof?
Hanafis consider 'urf a secondary source when no primary text exists.
3
Contrast with the case of the wasi
Why is the mudarib’s case different from the wasi’s? (Wasi restricted by orphan’s benefit; mudarib not so restricted).
The wasi must check if the drawee is wealthier than the debtor; the mudarib does not need to check.
4
Identify the underlying reason (illah)
What is the legal reason for the difference? (Mudarib is an agent with broad commercial discretion; wasi is a fiduciary bound by the ward’s welfare).
The mudarib’s authority is based on mutual business benefit, while the wasi’s is based on safeguarding the orphan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو احتال باالثمن ... الخ اگر مضارب نے کسی مالدار یا تنگدست پرشن کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی تاجروں کے یہاں معروف و معتاد ہے۔ بخلاف وصی کے کہ اگر اس نے مال یتیم کا حوالہ قبول کیا تو دیکھا جائے گا۔ کہ یہ یتیم کے حق میں بہتر ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر بہتر ہو۔ مثلاً جس پر حوالہ کیا گیا ہے وہ مدیون سے زیادہ مالدار ہوتو جائز ہوگا ورنہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ جبہ ظاہر ہے کہ وحی کا تصرف یتیم کی بہترائی کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔
His statement: 'And if he accepted a hawala for the price etc.' - If the mudarib accepted a hawala from a wealthy or a poor person, this is permissible because it is well-known and customary among traders. Unlike a wasi (guardian) who, if he accepts a hawala for the orphan's property, will be considered: if it is better for the orphan, e.g., the person who is the drawee is wealthier than the debtor, then it is permissible; otherwise not. The reason is that the wasi's authority is restricted by the orphan's benefit.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage rules that a mudarib may accept a hawala (transfer of debt) for the sale price, regardless of the debtor's wealth, because it is a common practice among merchants. The text contrasts this with a wasi (guardian of an orphan), who can only accept hawala if it benefits the orphan—specifically if the drawee (the person to whom the debt is transferred) is wealthier than the original debtor. The difference stems from the mudarib's greater discretion as a business partner, while the wasi's actions are strictly tied to the orphan's welfare.

Key Terms
حوالہ (ḥawālah): Transfer of debt from one person to another.
وصی (waṣī): Guardian of an orphan's property.
مضارب (muḍārib): The managing partner in a mudarabah contract.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom that is accepted as a source of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mudarib has explicit permission from the rabb al-mal.
B) Because it is customary among traders.
C) Because the poor debtor has a guarantor.
D) Because the mudarib assumes any loss.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib's authority to accept hawala is based on commercial custom, unlike a wasi who must consider the orphan's benefit.
