Three Types of Mudarib's Authority
Classification of mudarib's ownership of actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of a mudarib's authority and identify which actions require explicit permission from the rabb al-mal.

Core Idea
A mudarib's authority is tiered: ordinary trade is automatic, profit-sharing actions need 'act on your opinion', borrowing needs explicit consent.

The mudarabah contract grants the mudarib certain powers by default, but not all actions are included. This passage classifies the mudarib's authority into three distinct types, based on whether the action is inherent to trade, incidental to profit-making, or outside the scope of trade. Understanding this classification is crucial for both parties to avoid disputes and ensure valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first type
Actions the mudarib owns by the absolute contract itself, without any additional permission. These are ordinary trading acts like buying and selling goods.
2
Identify the second type
Actions he does not own by absolute contract but can perform if told 'act on your opinion'. Examples include re-mudarabah, mixing capitals, or forming partnerships. These are profit-enhancing but not essential.
The indication ('act on your opinion') includes these as they can be attached to trade.
3
Identify the third type
Actions he does not own even with that general permission, unless explicitly authorized. Primary example: borrowing (istidanah) to buy additional goods. Also includes non-trade acts like manumission, lending, gifting.
These actions change the capital amount or burden the rabb al-mal's liability.
4
Analyze the legal effect
If the rabb al-mal permits borrowing, the purchased goods become jointly owned half-half, similar to shirkat al-wujuh. This shows the legal consequence of explicit permission.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario involving a mudarib, determine which type of authority applies and whether the action is valid.
Practice with examples to solidify understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَوْعٌ لَا يَمْلِكُه بِمُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَيَمْلِكُهُ إِذَا قِيْلَ لَهُ اِعْمَلْ بِرَأيِكَ وَهُوَ مَا يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يُلْحَقَ بِهِ فَيَلْحَقُ عِنْدَ وُجُودِ الدَّلَالَةِ وَذَالِكَ مِثْلُ دَفْعِ الْمَالِ مُضَارَبَةً أَوْ شِرْكَةً إِلى غَيْرِهِ وَخَلْطُ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ بِمَالِهِ أَوْ بِمَالِ غَيْرِهِ لاَنَّ رَبَّ الْمَالِ رَضِيَ بِشِرْكَتِهِ لَا بِشِرُكَةِ غَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ أَمْرٌ عَارِضٌ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهِ التِّجَارَةُ فَلَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ مُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَلَكِنَّهُ جِهَةٌ فِى التَّثْمِيرِ فَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ يُوَافِقُهُ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ عِندَ وَجُودِ الدَّالَةِ وَقَوْلِهِ اِعْمَلْ بِرَايِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى ذَالِكَ وَنَوْعٍ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ لَا بِمُطْلَقِ الْعَقْدِ وَلَا بِقَوْلِهِ اِعْمَلْ بِرَايِكَ إِلَّا أَنَّ يَنْصُ عَلَيْهِ رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَهُوَ الْإِسْتِدَانَةِ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِى بِالدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ بَعْدَ مَا اشْتَرى بِرَأْسِ الْمَالِ السِّلْعَةِ وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَالِكَ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ الْمَالُ زَائِدَا عَلَى مَا الْعَقَدَ عَلَيْهِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ فَلَا يَرْضَى بِهِ وَلَا يُشْغِلُ ذِمَتَهُ بِالدَّيْنِ وَلَوْ أَذِنَ لَهُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ بِالْإِسْتِدَانَةِ صَارَ الْمُشْتَرِى بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ شِرْكَةِ الْوُجُوهِ وَاَخَذَ السَّفَاتِجِ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مِنَ الْإِسْتِدَانَةِ وَكَذَا إِعْطَاؤُهَا لِأَنَّهُ إِقْرَاضٌ وَالْعِتْقُ بِمَالٍ وَبِغَيْرِ مَالٍ وَالْكِتَابَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِتِجَارَةِ وَالْإِقْرَاضُ وَالْهِبَةُ وَالصَّدَقَةُ لأَنَّهُ تَبَرَّعَ مَحْضُ توضیح اللغة : خلط ملانا۔ تشمیر بڑھانا ۔ زیادہ کرنا۔ ینص (ن) نصا۔ نمایاں کرنا۔ استدانة قرض لینا۔ سلعة سامان تجارت۔ سفاتج جمع سفتجه، ہنڈی۔اقراض قرض دینا۔ ترجمہ اور ایک نوع دہ ہے جس کا مطلق عقد سے مالک نہیں ہوتا اور اس وقت مالک ہوتا ہے جب اس سے کہا گیا ہو کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کر۔ اور یہ وہ افعال ہیں جو تم اول کے ساتھ لاحق ہو سکتے۔ پس لاحق کئے جائیں گے دلالت ہونے کے وقت جیسے کسی کو مضاربت یا شرکت پر مال دینا اور مضاربت کو اپنے یا غیر کے مال سے خلط کرنا۔ کیونکہ مالک اس کی شرکت سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ غیر کی شرکت سے۔ اور یہ چونکہ امر عارض ہے جس پر تجارت موقوف نہیں اس لئے مطلق عقد کے تحت میں داخل نہ ہوں گے اور یہ کہنا کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کرنا داخل ہونے کے لئے دلالت کافی ہے اور ایک نوع وہ ہے جن کا مالک نہیں ہوتا نہ مطلق عقد سے اور نہ یہ کہنے سے کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کر ۔ مگر جب کہ رب المال اس کی تصریح کر دے۔ اور وہ ادھار لینا ہے جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ راس المال کے عوض اسباب خرید لینے کے بعد در اہم ودنا نیر یا ان کے مانند کیلی و وزنی چیز کے عوض خریدے۔ کیونکہ راس المال زائد ہوا جاتا ہے۔ اس سے جس پر مضاربت منعقد ہوئی تھی۔ پس مالک اس پر راضی نہ ہوگا اور نہ اپنے ذمہ کو قرض میں مشغول کرے گا۔ اور اگر مضارب کو رب المال نے ادھار لینے کی اجازت دے دی تو ادھار خریدی ہوئی چیز ان دونوں میں نصف نصف ہوگی بمنزلہ شرکت وجوہ کے۔ اور ہنڈی لینا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک قسم کا ادھار لینا ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ہنڈی دینا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ قرض دینا ہوتا ہے۔ اور عبد مضاربت کو مال پر یا بلا مال آزاد کرنا ہے اور مکاتب کرنا ہے کیونکہ یہ افعال تجارت سے نہیں ہیں اور قرض دینا، ہبہ کرنا صدقہ دینا ہے کیونکہ یہ سب احسان محض ہیں۔
And a type which he does not own by the absolute contract, but he owns it when it is said to him 'act on your opinion', and that is what can be attached to it, so it attaches when the indication exists. That is like giving the capital on mudarabah or partnership to another, and mixing the mudarabah capital with his own capital or with another's capital, because the rabb al-mal consented to his partnership, not to the partnership of another. And it is an incidental matter on which trade does not depend, so it does not fall under the absolute contract, but it is a means of profit-making, so from this aspect it agrees with it, thus it falls under it when the indication exists, and his statement 'act on your opinion' is an indication of that. And a type which he does not own, neither by the absolute contract nor by his statement 'act on your opinion', unless the rabb al-mal explicitly stipulates it, and that is borrowing (istidanah), which is that he buys with dirhams and dinars after having purchased the commodity with the capital, and similar things, because the capital becomes more than what the mudarabah was contracted upon, so he (the rabb al-mal) is not pleased with it, nor does he burden his liability with debt. If the rabb al-mal permits him to borrow, then what is bought becomes between them half-half, similar to partnership of faces (shirkat al-wujuh). And taking suftajah (bills of exchange) because it is a type of borrowing; similarly giving it, because it is lending. And freeing a slave for a consideration or without consideration, and kitabah (contract of manumission) because it is not trade; and lending, gifting, charity because they are pure donations.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the mudarib's authority. It identifies three types of actions: (1) Actions the mudarib owns by the absolute contract (not detailed here but implied, such as ordinary trading). (2) Actions he does not own by absolute contract but owns if told 'act on your opinion', such as giving mudarabah capital to another person (re-mudarabah), mixing the capital with his own or another's money, and entering into a partnership. These are secondary profit-making actions that require explicit indication of permission. (3) Actions he does not own even with that general permission, unless expressly authorized, such as taking loans (istidanah) to buy additional goods, because that increases the capital beyond the original amount and burdens the rabb al-mal's liability. Also included are non-trade acts like manumission, kitabah, lending, gifting, and charity. The text explains that if the rabb al-mal specifically permits borrowing, the purchased goods become jointly owned half and half, like shirkat al-wujuh (a credit partnership). This classification is essential for understanding the limits of a mudarib's implied authority.

Key Terms
مطلق العقد (muṭlaq al-ʿaqd): The general terms of the mudarabah contract without special conditions.
استدانة (istidānah): Borrowing money to purchase additional goods.
شركة الوجوه (shirkat al-wujūh): Partnership based on creditworthiness, without capital contribution.
سفاتج (sufātij): Bills of exchange or promissory notes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions does a mudarib NOT have authority to do even if told 'act on your opinion'?
A) Mixing mudarabah capital with his own money.
B) Giving the capital to another as mudarabah.
C) Taking a loan to buy more goods.
D) Selling goods at a profit.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib's authority has three tiers: automatic (trade), permission-dependent (profit-sharing actions), and explicit-only (borrowing and non-trade acts).

Mudarib Cannot Marry Slaves from Mudarabah Capital
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on marrying slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling regarding a mudarib arranging marriage for slaves and explain the reasoning of both the majority and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The mudarib is an agent for trade only; marriage is not trade, so it's not allowed.

This lesson examines a subtle boundary in mudarabah: can the mudarib arrange the marriage of a slave purchased with mudarabah capital? While Imam Abu Yusuf sees financial benefit, the majority restrict the mudarib's authority to trade alone. Understanding this dispute clarifies the scope of the mudarib's agency.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the mudarib cannot arrange marriage for any slave, male or female, from the mudarabah capital.
This is the majority position within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf allows the mudarib to marry a slave-girl because it is a form of acquisition (iktisab) – it brings mahr and reduces maintenance costs.
Abu Yusuf's position is based on financial benefit.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil: marriage results in acquisition (mahr) and expense reduction, similar to trade in benefits.
He broadens 'acquisition' to include non-trade benefits.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the majority's rebuttal: the mudarabah contract only authorizes trade (tijarah), not general acquisition. They analogize marriage to kitabah and freeing for money – both are acquisition but not trade, so they are excluded.
The key distinction is between trade and other forms of acquisition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the mudarib arranges marriage for a slave-girl, Abu Yusuf says it is valid; the majority say it is not permissible, and the mudarib may be liable.
The majority view is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يُزَوِّجُ عَبْدًا وَلَا اَمَةً مِنَ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يُزَوَّجُ الْآمَةَ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ الْإِكْتِسَابِ إِلَّا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَسْتَفِيدُ بِهِ الْمَهْرُ وَسُقُوطُ النَّفَقَةِ. وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِحِجَارَةٍ وَالْعَقْدُ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ إِلَّا التَّوْكِيْلَ بِالتِّجَارَةِ وَصَارِ كَالْكِتَابَةِ وَالْإِعْتَاقِ عَلَى مَالِ لِأَنَّهُ اكْتِسَابٌ وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنْ تِجَارَةً لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْمُصَارَبَةِ فَكَذَا هذَا ترجمہ اور نکاح نہ کرائے مال مضاربت کے کسی غلام یا باندی کا۔ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ باندی کو نکاح میں دے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ کمائی کے باب سے ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اس سے ہو مہر حاصل کرے گا اور نفقہ کا سقوط - طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تجارت نہیں ہے اور عقد مضاربت متضمن نہیں ہوتا تو کیل تجارت کے سوا کو تو یہ مکاتب کرنے اور مال پر آزاد کرنے کی طرح ہو گیا کہ یہ بھی اکتساب ہے۔ لیکن تجارت چونکہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے داخلِ مضاربت نہ ہوا ایسے ہی نکاح کرانا بھی داخل نہ ہوگا۔
He (the author) said: 'And he does not marry (i.e., arrange marriage for) a slave nor a slave-girl from the mudarabah capital.' And from Abu Yusuf that he may marry the slave-girl because it is from the type of acquisition. Do you not see that through it he obtains the dower and the fall of maintenance. And for them (the two, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) that it is not trade and the contract only includes agency for trade. And it becomes like kitabah and freeing for money, because it is acquisition, but since it is not trade, it does not fall under mudarabah; similarly this. Translation: And he should not arrange marriage for any slave or slave-girl from the mudarabah capital. From Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he may marry the slave-girl because it is from the bab of acquisition. Do you not see that through it he obtains the dower and the fall of maintenance. The argument of the two (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) is that it is not trade, and the mudarabah contract only includes agency for trade. So it becomes like kitabah and freeing for money, which are acquisition but since they are not trade, they do not fall under mudarabah; similarly this (marriage).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mudarib's authority to arrange the marriage of slaves owned in the mudarabah business. The matn states the mudarib cannot do so. Imam Abu Yusuf differs, allowing it for a slave-girl because it results in acquisition of dower and reduction of expenses. The response of the two (lahuma, referring to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually here 'lahuma' likely means Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as 'lahuma' often refers to the two companions against Abu Yusuf) is that marriage is not trade, and the mudarabah contract only authorizes trade. They analogize marriage to kitabah (contract of manumission) and freeing a slave for compensation—these are forms of acquisition but not trade, so they are not included. The majority view thus restricts the mudarib's actions to those that are essentially trading activities, not personal services like marriage.

Key Terms
اکتساب (iktisāb): Acquisition of wealth, broader than trade.
کتابة (kitābah): Contract of manumission where a slave pays for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, can a mudarib arrange the marriage of a slave-girl from the mudarabah capital?
A) Yes, because it brings in mahr.
B) No, because marriage is not trade.
C) Only if the slave-girl agrees.
D) Only if the rabb al-mal permits.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority is limited to trade; marriage is not trade, so it is not allowed.

Mudarib Giving Capital to Rabb al-Mal as Bida'ah: Agency or Retrieval?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of mudarabah when mudarib gives capital to rabb al-mal as bida'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority holds that giving mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah does not invalidate the original mudarabah, and identify the key distinction from a stipulation at the outset.

Core Idea
After takhliyah, the mudarib owns the right to trade; the rabb al-mal becomes his agent, not a retriever.

This lesson examines a subtle scenario in mudarabah where the mudarib gives some capital to the rabb al-mal to trade on his behalf as bida'ah. The majority Hanafi position upholds the validity of the original mudarabah, while Imam Zufar argues it becomes invalid. Understanding the reasoning hinges on the concept of takhliyah and the nature of agency.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the majority ruling
Identify that the mudarib gives part of the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah. The matn rules that the mudarabah remains valid.
2
Understand Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that the rabb al-mal cannot be an agent in his own property; thus, receiving capital is retrieval (istirdad), making the mudarabah fasid.
3
Analyze the majority's response
The majority respond that takhliyah (handover) has already occurred, so the mudarib has the right of disposal. Hence, the rabb al-mal can act as the mudarib's agent, not as a retriever.
Key concept: takhliyah transfers control.
4
Distinguish from analogous cases
Contrast this with (a) stipulating work on rabb al-mal at the outset (invalid because it prevents takhliyah) and (b) giving capital as a second mudarabah (invalid because mudarib has no capital).
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If Zufar's view is taken, the mudarabah becomes fasid, requiring restructuring. Under the majority, it remains valid, and profits are shared according to the original contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ دَفَعَ شَيْئًا مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِضَاعَةً فَاشْتَرَى رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَبَاعَ فَهُوَ عَلَى الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقَالَ زُفَرٌّ تَفْسُهُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لِاَنَّ رَبَّ الْمَالِ مُتَصَرِّقْ فِى مَالِ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يُصْلَحُ وَكِيلًا فِيهِ فَيَصِيرُ مُسْتَرِدًا وَلِهَذَا لَا يَصِحُ إِذَا شَرَطَ الْعَمَلَ عَلَيْهِ ابْتِدَاءً وَلَنَا أَنَّ التَّخْلِيَةَ فِيْهِ قَدْ تَمَّتْ وَصَارَ التَّصَرُّفَ حَقًّا لِلْمُصَارِبِ فَيَصْلُحُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَكِيلًا عَنْهُ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ وَالْإِبْصَاعُ تَوْكِيْلُ مِنْهُ فَلَا يَكُونُ إِسْتِرْدَدًا بِخِلَافِ شَرْطِ الْعَمَلِ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْإِبْتِدَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ التَّخْلِيَةَ وَبِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا دَفَعَ الْمَالَ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ مُضَارَبَةً حَيْثُ لَا يَصِحُ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارَبَةَ تَنْعَقِدُ شِرْكَةُ عَلَى مَالِ رَبِّ الْمَالِ وَعَمِلَ الْمُضَارِبِ وَلَا مَالَ هَهُنَا لِلْمُضَارِبِ فَلَوْ جَوَّزْنَاهُ يُؤْدِى إِلَى قَلْبِ الْمُوْضُوع وَإِذَا لَمْ يَصِحُ بَقِيَ عَمَلُ رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِأَمْرِ الْمُضَارِبِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِهِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ الأولى ترجمہ اگر مضارب نے کچھ مال مضاربت رب المال کو بضاعت پر دیا پس رب المال نے خرید و فروخت کی تو یہ مضاربت پر ہوگا۔ امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ مضاربت فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ رب المال اپنے ذاتی مال میں متصرف ہے تو وہ اس میں وکیل نہیں ہو سکتا پس وہ واپس لینے والا ہو گیا اسی لئے مضاربت صحیح نہیں ہوتی اگر ابتداء میں رب المال کے ذمہ کام کرنا
He said: 'If he gives something from the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah, and the rabb al-mal buys and sells, it remains on mudarabah.' And Zufar said: The mudarabah becomes fasid (invalid), because the rabb al-mal is acting in his own property, so he cannot be an agent in it, thus he becomes a retriever (mustaridd). For this reason, it is not valid if he (the rabb al-mal) stipulates the work on himself initially. Our argument: the handover (takhliyah) has been completed, and the right of disposal has become the right of the mudarib, so the rabb al-mal can be an agent for him in disposal, and the bida'ah is his agency, so it is not a retrieval. This is unlike stipulating the work on him initially, because that prevents takhliyah. And unlike the case where he gives the capital to the rabb al-mal as mudarabah (which is invalid), because mudarabah requires capital from the rabb al-mal and work from the mudarib, and here the mudarib has no capital, so if we allowed it, it would reverse the subject. And when the first is invalid, the work of the rabb al-mal by the mudarib's command remains, so the first mudarabah is not nullified.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the majority Hanafis and Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) regarding a scenario where the mudarib gives some of the mudarabah capital back to the rabb al-mal with instructions to trade on his behalf as bida'ah (an investment without profit-sharing). The matn rules that the mudarabah continues, and the rabb al-mal's transactions are counted for the mudarabah. Zufar argues that this invalidates the mudarabah because the rabb al-mal is dealing with his own property and cannot be the mudarib's agent. The majority response is that the mudarib has already taken possession (takhliyah), so the right to trade belongs to the mudarib; thus, the rabb al-mal can act as the mudarib's agent. This is different from a stipulation at the outset (which would make it invalid) or from giving the capital as a second mudarabah to the rabb al-mal (which would also be invalid). The distinction is that here the mudarib retains control, and the rabb al-mal is merely his agent.

Key Terms
بضاعة (biḍāʿah): A type of investment where the agent trades on behalf of the owner without profit-sharing.
تخلیة (takhliyah): Handover of capital to the mudarib, giving him possession.
استرداد (istirdād): Retrieval or taking back of capital by the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, if a mudarib gives some mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah and the rabb al-mal trades, what is the status of the original mudarabah?
A) It becomes fasid.
B) It remains valid.
C) It becomes a new mudarabah.
D) It is void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
After takhliyah, the mudarib may appoint the rabb al-mal as his agent without invalidating the mudarabah, provided it is not a stipulation at the outset.

Actions Not Permitted in Mudarabah Without Explicit Authorization
Listing prohibited actions in mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the actions a mudarib cannot perform without explicit authorization and explain the Hanafi rationale for each category.

Core Idea
In mudarabah, the mudarib's authority is limited to trade; any act outside trade requires the capital owner's explicit permission.

Mudarabah is a contract where one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib) to trade for profit. But what exactly can the mudarib do? The Hanafi school strictly limits the mudarib's authority to actual trade. This lesson clarifies which actions are not permitted without explicit permission, helping you avoid common pitfalls in practice.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two categories of actions
The text separates actions that can be attached with an indication (like 'act on your opinion') from those requiring explicit permission. Identify the criteria: the first category involves actions where the owner's implicit consent can be inferred; the second involves actions that are not trade and cannot be inferred.
2
Examine the first category: actions attachable with indication
These include mixing the mudarabah capital with the mudarib's own funds or giving some capital to another person for mudarabah or partnership. They can be included if the rabb al-mal says 'act on your opinion' or similar. The rationale is that these are accidental and trade does not depend on them.
The owner agreed to the mudarib's partnership, not another's.
3
Examine the second category: actions requiring explicit permission
These include buying on credit, taking or giving hundis (bills of exchange), freeing slaves, making kitabah, giving loans, gifts, and charity. They are not considered trade because they either involve credit/debt or are pure beneficence. They require the rabb al-mal to explicitly allow them.
Even with 'act on your opinion', these are not included unless explicitly stated.
4
Understand the legal consequence
If a mudarib performs any of these unauthorized actions and incurs a loss, he is personally liable. The rabb al-mal is not bound. This protects the capital owner's investment.
If credit is authorized, goods bought on credit are shared half-and-half between rabb al-mal and mudarib, like a credit partnership (shirkat al-wujuh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہ وہ افعال ہیں جو تم اول کے ساتھ لاحق ہو سکتے۔ پس لاحق کئے جائیں گے دلالت ہونے کے وقت جیسے کسی کو مضاربت یا شرکت پر مال دینا اور مضاربت کو اپنے یا غیر کے مال سے خلط کرنا۔ کیونکہ مالک اس کی شرکت سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ غیر کی شرکت سے۔ اور یہ چونکہ امر عارض ہے جس پر تجارت موقوف نہیں اس لئے مطلق عقد کے تحت میں داخل نہ ہوں گے اور یہ کہنا کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کرنا داخل ہونے کے لئے دلالت کافی ہے اور ایک نوع وہ ہے جن کا مالک نہیں ہوتا نہ مطلق عقد سے اور نہ یہ کہنے سے کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کر ۔ مگر جب کہ رب المال اس کی تصریح کر دے۔ اور وہ ادھار لینا ہے جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ راس المال کے عوض اسباب خرید لینے کے بعد در اہم ودنا نیر یا ان کے مانند کیلی و وزنی چیز کے عوض خریدے۔ کیونکہ راس المال زائد ہوا جاتا ہے۔ اس سے جس پر مضاربت منعقد ہوئی تھی۔ پس مالک اس پر راضی نہ ہوگا اور نہ اپنے ذمہ کو قرض میں مشغول کرے گا۔ اور اگر مضارب کو رب المال نے ادھار لینے کی اجازت دے دی تو ادھار خریدی ہوئی چیز ان دونوں میں نصف نصف ہوگی بمنزلہ شرکت وجوہ کے۔ اور ہنڈی لینا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک قسم کا ادھار لینا ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ہنڈی دینا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ قرض دینا ہوتا ہے۔ اور عبد مضاربت کو مال پر یا بلا مال آزاد کرنا ہے اور مکاتب کرنا ہے کیونکہ یہ افعال تجارت سے نہیں ہیں اور قرض دینا، ہبہ کرنا صدقہ دینا ہے کیونکہ یہ سب احسان محض ہیں۔
These are the actions that can be attached to the first [type]. They will be attached when there is an indication, such as giving money to someone for mudarabah or partnership, and mixing mudarabah capital with one's own or another's wealth. Because the owner agreed to his partnership, not to another's. And since this is an accidental matter on which trade does not depend, it will not be included under the absolute contract. And saying 'act according to your opinion' is sufficient indication for inclusion. And there is a type that is not owned by the absolute contract nor by saying 'act according to your opinion', unless the rabb al-mal explicitly specifies it. And that is taking on credit, which takes the form of buying goods in exchange for the capital, then buying [something else] in exchange for dirhams and dananir or similar measurable/weighable items. Because the capital increases, [deviating] from what the mudarabah was contracted upon. So the owner will not be pleased with this, nor will he engage his liability in debt. And if the rabb al-mal permitted the mudarib to take on credit, then the goods bought on credit will be half-and-half between them, like a partnership in credit (shirkat al-wujuh). And taking a hundi [bill of exchange] is also [not permitted] because it is a type of credit. Similarly, giving a hundi is [not permitted] because it is giving a loan. And freeing a slave of the mudarabah with or without money, and making a kitabah contract, because these actions are not trade. And giving a loan, making a gift, giving charity, because these are pure favors.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing actions that a mudarib (manager) cannot undertake within the mudarabah contract without explicit permission from the rabb al-mal (capital owner). The text distinguishes two types: actions that can be included if there is an indication (like mixing capital or giving money to another for mudarabah/partnership) and actions that require explicit permission (like buying on credit, taking/giving hundis, freeing slaves, making kitabah, lending, gifting, and giving charity). The rationale is that these actions are not trade (tijarah) but rather acts of beneficence or credit, and the mudarabah contract is specifically for trade. If the mudarib does any of these without authorization, he may be liable. The Hanafi position is clear: without explicit permission, these acts are not covered by the absolute mudarabah contract.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership in profit where one party provides capital and the other provides labor/trade skill.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital owner who provides funds for the mudarabah.
مضارب (mudarib): The manager/worker who uses the capital for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions does NOT require explicit permission from rabb al-mal in a mudarabah contract?
A) Freeing a slave from mudarabah capital
B) Lending mudarabah capital to someone
C) Mixing mudarabah capital with one's own money
D) Giving a loan from mudarabah capital

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority is strictly limited to trade; any act outside this must be explicitly authorized by the capital owner.

Marrying Slaves from Mudarabah Capital: Dispute with Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudarib's authority to marry slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on marrying off slaves from mudarabah capital and explain why Abu Yusuf's contrary view is not adopted, citing the distinction between acquisition (iktisab) and trade (tijarah).

Core Idea
Mudarabah authorizes trade, not all acquisition – marrying off a slave is acquisition, not trade, so it is not permitted.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of the mudarib's authority. While Abu Yusuf argued that marrying off a female slave from mudarabah capital is permissible because it yields dower and saves maintenance (a form of acquisition), the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintained that the mudarabah contract only authorizes trade. Understanding the distinction between acquisition (iktisab) and trade (tijarah) is critical to defining the boundaries of the mudarib's lawful actions.

Guided Path
1
State the majority opinion and its basis
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the mudarib cannot marry off a male or female slave from mudarabah capital. The basis is that the contract only authorizes trade (tijarah), not any acquisition.
The majority view is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
2
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's view and his proof
Note that Abu Yusuf permits marrying off a female slave only, reasoning that it falls under acquisition (iktisab) because it brings dower and saves maintenance costs.
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the key distinction: iktisab vs. tijarah
Recognize that the majority refutes Abu Yusuf by distinguishing between acquisition and trade. While marriage yields acquisition, it is not trade. The mudarabah contract is explicitly limited to trade (authorization to buy and sell).
This distinction is a recurring theme in Hanafi mudarabah law.
4
Examine the analogy to kitabah and itq
The majority draws an analogy: making a kitabah contract or freeing a slave for money is also acquisition but not trade; therefore it is not allowed in mudarabah. Similarly, marrying a slave is acquisition but not trade.
This qiyas strengthens the ruling by showing a consistent principle.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a mudarib marries off a slave without permission, he is liable for any loss, and the dower (if received) is not considered partnership profit. This creates a clear practical difference between the two positions.
The thamarah al-khilaf ensures that the dispute has real-world implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يُزَوِّجُ عَبْدًا وَلَا اَمَةً مِنَ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يُزَوَّجُ الْآمَةَ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ الْإِكْتِسَابِ إِلَّا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَسْتَفِيدُ بِهِ الْمَهْرُ وَسُقُوطُ النَّفَقَةِ. وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِحِجَارَةٍ وَالْعَقْدُ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ إِلَّا التَّوْكِيْلَ بِالتِّجَارَةِ وَصَارِ كَالْكِتَابَةِ وَالْإِعْتَاقِ عَلَى مَالِ لِأَنَّهُ اكْتِسَابٌ وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنْ تِجَارَةً لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْمُصَارَبَةِ فَكَذَا هذَا قَالَ فَإِنْ دَفَعَ شَيْئًا مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِضَاعَةً فَاشْتَرَى رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَبَاعَ فَهُوَ عَلَى الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقَالَ زُفَرٌّ تَفْسُهُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لِاَنَّ رَبَّ الْمَالِ مُتَصَرِّقْ فِى مَالِ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يُصْلَحُ وَكِيلًا فِيهِ فَيَصِيرُ مُسْتَرِدًا وَلِهَذَا لَا يَصِحُ إِذَا شَرَطَ الْعَمَلَ عَلَيْهِ ابْتِدَاءً وَلَنَا أَنَّ التَّخْلِيَةَ فِيْهِ قَدْ تَمَّتْ وَصَارَ التَّصَرُّفَ حَقًّا لِلْمُصَارِبِ فَيَصْلُحُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَكِيلًا عَنْهُ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ وَالْإِبْصَاعُ تَوْكِيْلُ مِنْهُ فَلَا يَكُونُ إِسْتِرْدَدًا بِخِلَافِ شَرْطِ الْعَمَلِ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْإِبْتِدَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ التَّخْلِيَةَ وَبِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا دَفَعَ الْمَالَ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ مُضَارَبَةً حَيْثُ لَا يَصِحُ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارَبَةَ تَنْعَقِدُ شِرْكَةُ عَلَى مَالِ رَبِّ الْمَالِ وَعَمِلَ الْمُضَارِبِ وَلَا مَالَ هَهُنَا لِلْمُضَارِبِ فَلَوْ جَوَّزْنَاهُ يُؤْدِى إِلَى قَلْبِ الْمُوْضُوع وَإِذَا لَمْ يَصِحُ بَقِيَ عَمَلُ رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِأَمْرِ الْمُضَارِبِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِهِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ الأولى
He said: And he should not marry off a male slave nor a female slave from the mudarabah capital. And from Abu Yusuf that he marries off the female slave because it is from the category of acquisition. Do you not see that through it he acquires the dower and the falling away of maintenance? And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) [the proof] is that it is not trade, and the contract does not include except authorization for trade. And it is like making a kitabah contract and freeing [a slave] in exchange for money, because that is acquisition, but since it is not trade, it does not enter under the mudarabah. So this is likewise. He said: Then if he gives something from the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as a bida'ah (consignment), and the rabb al-mal buys and sells, then it is upon the mudarabah. And Zufar said: The mudarabah becomes void because the rabb al-mal is a disposer in his own property, so he cannot be an agent in it, thus he becomes a retractor. For this reason, it is not valid if the work upon him is stipulated initially. And for us [the proof] is that the relinquishment (takhliyah) in it has been completed, and disposal has become the right of the mudarib, so the rabb al-mal can be an agent for him in disposal. And giving as bida'ah is authorization from him, so it is not a retraction. Unlike the stipulation of work upon him initially, because it prevents takhliyah. And unlike when he gives the capital to the rabb al-mal as a mudarabah, where it is not valid because mudarabah is contracted as a partnership on the capital of the rabb al-mal and the work of the mudarib, and there is no capital here from the mudarib. So if we allowed it, it would lead to inversion of the subject. And when it is not valid, the work of the rabb al-mal remains by the order of the mudarib, so the first mudarabah is not invalidated thereby.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage covers two intra-Hanafi disputes. First, regarding marrying off slaves: The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that a mudarib cannot marry off a slave (male or female) from mudarabah capital, because that is not trade. Abu Yusuf reports that a female slave may be married off, as it results in acquiring dower and saving maintenance, which is a form of acquisition. However, the majority respond that while it is acquisition, it is not trade, and the mudarabah contract only authorizes trade. Thus, it is like making a kitabah contract or freeing a slave for money — acquisition but not trade. Second, regarding giving capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah: The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that if the mudarib gives some mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah (consignment) and the rabb al-mal trades with it, the mudarabah remains valid. Zufar argues that the mudarabah becomes void because the rabb al-mal is acting in his own property and cannot be an agent. The majority counter that after takhliyah (relinquishment), the right of disposal belongs to the mudarib, so the rabb al-mal can be his agent. The bida'ah is a form of authorization, not a retraction. The commentary clarifies that this is not like stipulating work on the rabb al-mal initially, nor like giving capital as a separate mudarabah.

Key Terms
اكْتِسَاب (iktisab): Acquisition of wealth or benefit, broader than trade.
تِجَارَة (tijarah): Trade, specifically buying and selling for profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, why is marrying off a female slave from mudarabah capital not permitted?
A) Because it does not yield any profit
B) Because it is not a form of trade (tijarah)
C) Because it requires the slave's consent
D) Because it may lead to loss of capital

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi mudarabah, the mudarib's authority is limited to trade; non-trade acquisitions, even if beneficial, are not permitted.

Bida'ah: Mudarib Giving Capital to Rabb al-Mal for Trading
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of mudarabah when mudarib gives capital to rabb al-mal as bida'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib giving mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah for him to trade with, and explain why the mudarabah remains valid, contrary to Zufar's view.

Core Idea
When a mudarib entrusts capital to the rabb al-mal as a consignment (bida'ah), the mudarabah continues because the rabb al-mal acts as the mudarib's agent, not as owner.

This lesson covers a second intra-Hanafi dispute arising from the same passage: if the mudarib gives some of the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal (the capital owner) as a bida'ah (consignment) and the rabb al-mal trades with it, does the original mudarabah become void? Zufar argued that it becomes void because the rabb al-mal cannot be an agent in his own property. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) held that the mudarabah remains valid. Understanding the concept of takhliyah (relinquishment) and agency clarifies why the rabb al-mal can act as the mudarib's agent.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the majority ruling
The mudarib gives some of the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as a bida'ah (consignment). The rabb al-mal then trades with it. The majority rule that the mudarabah remains valid and the transactions are on account of the mudarabah.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Present Zufar's opposing view and his proof
Zufar argues that the mudarabah becomes void because the rabb al-mal is dealing in his own property; he cannot be an agent for the mudarib. Therefore, the rabb al-mal is effectively retracting the capital.
Zufar's view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
3
Explain the majority's rebuttal: takhliyah and agency
The majority respond that after the mudarib takes possession (takhliyah), the right of disposal belongs to the mudarib. The rabb al-mal can then act as the mudarib's agent in trading. The bida'ah is an authorization (tawkil) from the mudarib, not a retraction.
The key is that takhliyah transfers disposal rights to the mudarib, so the rabb al-mal's later actions are on behalf of the mudarib.
4
Distinguish from prohibited scenarios
The majority note two exceptions: (1) if the work is stipulated on the rabb al-mal initially, it is invalid because it prevents takhliyah. (2) If the mudarib gives capital to the rabb al-mal as a new mudarabah (rather than bida'ah), it is invalid because the rabb al-mal would be both owner and worker, inverting the structure.
These distinctions show the boundaries of the ruling.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the bida'ah arrangement is allowed, the mudarabah continues, and any profit from the rabb al-mal's trades is shared according to the original contract. If void (per Zufar), the rabb al-mal's trades would be for himself, and the mudarabah would end.
The majority view preserves the partnership and avoids unnecessary invalidation.

Source Text

Key Terms
تَخْلِيَة (takhliyah): The act of relinquishing possession and control to the mudarib, after which the mudarib has the right to dispose of the capital.
بِضَاعَة (bida'ah): A consignment where goods or capital are given to another to trade with, but the recipient does not share in profit; it is a form of agency.
اِسْتِرْدَاد (istirdad): Retraction; taking back the capital and thus ending the mudarabah.

Key Takeaway
After takhliyah, the mudarib may authorize the rabb al-mal to trade as his agent via bida'ah without invalidating the original mudarabah.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Mudarib Giving Capital to Rabb al-Mal as Bida'ah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of mudarabah after bida'ah transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the validity of mudarabah when the mudarib gives capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah, and distinguish it from Zufar's view.

Core Idea
After takhliyah, the mudarib's authorization keeps the mudarabah valid even if the rabb al-mal trades the capital as bida'ah.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to a mudarabah contract when the mudarib returns some capital to the rabb al-mal as a bida'ah (consignment) and the rabb al-mal trades with it? Zufar argues the mudarabah becomes void, but the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it remains valid. The key analytical concept is takhliyah (relinquishment of control), which determines who holds the right of disposal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ikhtilaf
Recognize the scenario: the mudarib gives some mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah, and the rabb al-mal trades with it. The dispute is whether the original mudarabah remains valid.
This is a operational act (trading by rabb al-mal) that could affect the mudarabah's status.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
The three imams rule that the mudarabah remains valid. The rabb al-mal's trades are performed on behalf of the mudarabah, so profits are shared per the original contract.
The majority view is mufta bihi.
3
Analyze Zufar's dalil
Zufar argues that the rabb al-mal is acting in his own property (as owner), cannot be an agent for the mudarib, and by taking the capital he effectively retracts the mudarabah.
Zufar analogizes to the case where work on the rabb al-mal is stipulated initially (invalid).
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The majority rebut that takhliyah has already been completed, giving the mudarib the right of disposal. The mudarib's act of giving as bida'ah is a form of authorization (tawkil), not retraction. The rabb al-mal can validly act as the mudarib's agent.
This distinguishes from the initial stipulation case (where takhliyah is prevented) and from giving capital as a new mudarabah (which would invert the subject).
5
Determine the thamarah and mufta bihi
If Zufar's view were followed, profits from the rabb al-mal's trades would belong solely to him, voiding the profit-sharing. The majority view preserves the original profit-sharing. The majority view is the relied-upon position.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: profit distribution depends on whose view is applied.

قَالَ فَإِنْ دَفَعَ شَيْئًا مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِضَاعَةً فَاشْتَرَى رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَبَاعَ فَهُوَ عَلَى الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقَالَ زُفَرٌّ تَفْسُهُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لِاَنَّ رَبَّ الْمَالِ مُتَصَرِّقْ فِى مَالِ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يُصْلَحُ وَكِيلًا فِيهِ فَيَصِيرُ مُسْتَرِدًا وَلِهَذَا لَا يَصِحُ إِذَا شَرَطَ الْعَمَلَ عَلَيْهِ ابْتِدَاءً وَلَنَا أَنَّ التَّخْلِيَةَ فِيْهِ قَدْ تَمَّتْ وَصَارَ التَّصَرُّفَ حَقًّا لِلْمُصَارِبِ فَيَصْلُحُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ وَكِيلًا عَنْهُ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ وَالْإِبْصَاعُ تَوْكِيْلُ مِنْهُ فَلَا يَكُونُ إِسْتِرْدَدًا بِخِلَافِ شَرْطِ الْعَمَلِ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْإِبْتِدَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ التَّخْلِيَةَ وَبِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا دَفَعَ الْمَالَ إِلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ مُضَارَبَةً حَيْثُ لَا يَصِحُ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارَبَةَ تَنْعَقِدُ شِرْكَةُ عَلَى مَالِ رَبِّ الْمَالِ وَعَمِلَ الْمُضَارِبِ وَلَا مَالَ هَهُنَا لِلْمُضَارِبِ فَلَوْ جَوَّزْنَاهُ يُؤْدِى إِلَى قَلْبِ الْمُوْضُوع وَإِذَا لَمْ يَصِحُ بَقِيَ عَمَلُ رَبِّ الْمَالِ بِأَمْرِ الْمُضَارِبِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِهِ الْمُضَارَبَةُ الأولى
He said: Then if he gives something from the mudarabah capital to the rabb al-mal as a bida'ah, and the rabb al-mal buys and sells, then it is upon the mudarabah. And Zufar said: The mudarabah becomes void because the rabb al-mal is a disposer in his own property, so he cannot be an agent in it, thus he becomes a retractor. For this reason, it is not valid if the work upon him is stipulated initially. And for us [the proof] is that the relinquishment (takhliyah) in it has been completed, and disposal has become the right of the mudarib, so the rabb al-mal can be an agent for him in disposal. And giving as bida'ah is authorization from him, so it is not a retraction. Unlike the stipulation of work upon him initially, because it prevents takhliyah. And unlike when he gives the capital to the rabb al-mal as a mudarabah, where it is not valid because mudarabah is contracted as a partnership on the capital of the rabb al-mal and the work of the mudarib, and there is no capital here from the mudarib. So if we allowed it, it would lead to inversion of the subject. And when it is not valid, the work of the rabb al-mal remains by the order of the mudarib, so the first mudarabah is not invalidated thereby.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scenario where a mudarib gives some of the mudarabah capital back to the rabb al-mal as a bida'ah (consignment, i.e., for the rabb al-mal to trade with on behalf of the mudarabah). The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the original mudarabah remains valid, and any trading done by the rabb al-mal with that capital is on behalf of the mudarabah. Zufar argues that the mudarabah becomes void because the rabb al-mal is acting in his own property and cannot be an agent; thus, by accepting the capital, he effectively retracts the mudarabah. The majority respond that after the mudarib has taken possession (takhliyah tamm), the right of disposal belongs to the mudarib. Therefore, the rabb al-mal can act as the mudarib's agent. The bida'ah is a form of authorization (tawkil) from the mudarib, not a retraction. This differs from two cases: (1) if work on the rabb al-mal was stipulated initially, that prevents takhliyah and invalidates the mudarabah from the start; (2) if the mudarib gives the capital to the rabb al-mal as a separate mudarabah, that is invalid because the rabb al-mal cannot be both capital owner and manager of a new mudarabah with his own capital. In the present case, since the first mudarabah is valid, the rabb al-mal's work by the mudarib's order does not nullify it.

Key Terms
بضاعة (bida'ah): Consignment: giving goods or capital to another to trade with on behalf of the giver, without partnership in profit (the trader receives a fee or gift).
تخلیة (takhliyah): Relinquishment or handing over of capital by the rabb al-mal to the mudarib, giving him full control over disposal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, why does the mudarabah remain valid when the mudarib gives capital to the rabb al-mal as bida'ah?
A) Because the rabb al-mal remains the owner of the capital
B) Because takhliyah has been completed and the mudarib authorizes the rabb al-mal as an agent
C) Because the bida'ah is a new contract that supersedes the mudarabah
D) Because the rabb al-mal cannot be an agent

Key Takeaway
The completion of takhliyah gives the mudarib authority to authorize the rabb al-mal as an agent via bida'ah, preserving the mudarabah's validity – a key distinction from Zufar's void ruling.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
6 min
Mudarib's Authority Regarding Marriage of Slaves
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudarib's authority over slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on the mudarib's authority to marry slaves, cite the opposing view of Imam Abu Yusuf, and explain the talil (analogical reasoning) that restricts mudarabah to trade.

Core Idea
The mudarib cannot marry slaves because mudarabah is limited to trade and marriage is not trade.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the scope of a mudarib's authority over slaves owned by the mudarabah capital. The central question is whether the mudarib may arrange marriages for these slaves, as marriage can yield profit (dower) and reduce maintenance expenses. We will explore the majority position shared by Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the exceptional view attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, and the analogical reasoning (talil) that ultimately confines mudarabah activities to genuine trade.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi ruling
Identify the default ruling as presented in the passage: the mudarib has no authority to give a male slave permission to marry or to give a female slave in marriage. This sets the baseline for the dispute.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab exception
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold an exceptional view: the mudarib may marry off a slave-girl in exchange for dower because it yields profit and removes maintenance expenses.
This is a riwayah from Abu Yusuf, not necessarily his final or mufta bihi view.
3
Trace the proof for the majority
Examine the majority's argument: although marriage yields dower, it is not trade, and the mudarabah contract is restricted to trade. The analogy (talil) is drawn to making a slave a mukatab or freeing him for money — these also generate profit but are not trade.
The common illa (effective cause) is that the act is not trade, even if profitable.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: under Abu Yusuf's view, the dower becomes part of the mudarabah profit; under the majority, the marriage is invalid for the mudarabah, and the dower belongs to the capital owner (rabb al-maal), not the mudarabah fund.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The mudarib cannot marry slaves within the mudarabah contract.

تشریح قوله ولا يزوج عبدا الخ- مضارب کو اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے کہ مالِ مضاربت کے کسی غلام کو نکاح کرنے کی اجازت دے یا باندی کو کسی کے نکاح میں دے۔ اور تو اور میں امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ باندی کو مہر کے عوض نکاح میں دے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی ایک طرح کی کمائی ہے کہ اس فعل سے مضارب کو مہر حاصل ہوگا اور اس کے ذمہ سے نفقہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ سب تو تسلیم ہے۔ مگر یہ تجارت نہیں ہے اور عقد مضاربت تو کیل تجارت کے علاوہ کسی اور طریق سے کمائی کو شامل نہیں۔ پس باندی کا نکاح کرنا ایسا ہو گیا کہ جیسے مضاربت کے غلام کو مکاتب کرنا یا اس کو مال کے عوض آزاد کرنا کہ اس سے بھی مال حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ تجارت سے نہیں ہے اس لئے داخلِ مضاربت نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی تزویج امت بھی داخل نہ ہوگی۔
Explanation of his saying: 'And he does not marry a slave...' The mudarib does not have the authority to permit any male slave of the mudarabah capital to marry, nor to give a female slave in marriage to anyone. And in [one narration] it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that he can give the female slave in marriage in exchange for dower, because this is also a kind of earning, as by this act the mudarib will obtain dower and the maintenance expense will be removed from his liability. The proof of the two sides [i.e., the majority] is: all this is conceded, but it is not trade, and the mudarabah contract only includes earning through trade, not through any other means. Thus marrying the female slave becomes like making a mudarabah slave a mukatab or freeing him for money, which also yields money. But since it is not trade, it is not included in mudarabah, so similarly the marriage of a slave-girl is not included.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mudarib's authority over the slaves of the mudarabah capital. The ruling: the mudarib cannot arrange marriages for the slaves (male or female) of the mudarabah capital because the mudarabah contract is limited to trade, and marriage is not trade. Imam Abu Yusuf narrates a view that the mudarib may marry off a slave-girl in exchange for dower, as this yields profit (dower) and relieves the mudarib of her maintenance. However, the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and the relied-upon position) hold that this is not allowed, as the contract only authorizes trade; any non-trade profit is outside the scope of mudarabah, analogous to making a slave a mukatab or freeing him for payment—these are not trade and thus not part of mudarabah. The commentator follows the order: first states the general ruling, then presents Abu Yusuf's exception, then the opposing proof that marriage is not trade, concluding that the majority view is correct.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The managing partner in a mudarabah contract who invests the capital with his labor.
رب المال (rabb al-maal): The capital provider in a mudarabah contract.
بضاعت (bida'at): Here, a type of investment where capital is given to another for trading without sharing profit, often as a loan or consignment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, why can the mudarib not marry off a slave-girl of the mudarabah capital?
A) Because the mudarib has no right over the slaves at all.
B) Because marriage is not considered trade, and mudarabah is limited to trade.
C) Because the dower is too uncertain.
D) Because the owner's permission is required for any act.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority is strictly limited to trade; marriage and similar non-trade acts are outside the scope of mudarabah.
